New Stamp Tax Law to be Implemented Tomorrow; City Chamber of Commerce Indicates Key Points; Matters to Note During the Transition

The new stamp tax law is now scheduled to be implemented on September 1. All stamp affixing methods from September 1 will also be handled in accordance with the new law. However, during this transition period, there are several points to note that merchants and manufacturers must understand. Here, Yan Ersheng, the secretary of the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, explained each point as follows:

Receipts for Goods: According to the old stamp tax method, it was originally not necessary to affix stamps for receipts for goods. However, the new law stipulates that a receipt for goods worth 3 yuan or more must be affixed with 1 fen, 10 yuan or more must be affixed with 1 fen, and 100 yuan or more must be affixed with 3 fen, up to 3 fen, with no further stamps required. The return receipts for letters usually used by stores and factories are receipts for sending letters and do not need to be stamped according to law. However, if it is noted outside the letter that several items of goods have been sent, then this return receipt should be stamped. Therefore, in addition to purely return receipts for letters, it is appropriate to affix stamps. As for the delivery return receipts used before September 1, they should be stamped according to law from September 1 and cannot be resisted on the grounds that the ledger was established before September 1. However, old ledgers that have been affixed with a 1-jiao stamp can be used until the closing of accounts. There is no need to affix additional stamps at this time. However, new ledgers opened after September 1 should be affixed with 2 jiao. Also, the explanation under the receipts for silver, money, and goods in the tax rate table has the sentence "except for deposit receipts from the financial industry." The meaning of this sentence is that the stamp affixing method for deposit receipts from the financial industry is separately stipulated in item 4 and item 9, etc. It does not mean that deposit receipts from the financial industry do not need to be stamped.

Petitions from the People: Petitions from the people submitted to government offices should be affixed with a 1-jiao stamp in accordance with category 3 of article 2 of the old regulations. However, the new stamp tax law does not have this provision and should be exempt from stamping. Also, petitions for requesting naturalization are also exempt from stamp duty under the new law.

Bill Reminders: Bill reminders were not required to be stamped according to the temporary regulations on stamp duty, but the Ministry later stipulated that they should be stamped. However, the new law stipulates that they are exempt from stamping. However, the explanation of bill reminders is stipulated in article 5 of the implementing rules, which refers to bill reminders used for the New Year's festival, which only list the amount owed. The bills that are customarily listed by name, quantity, value, and delivered to customers on a monthly or annual basis, such as the bills from clothing stores, should still be stamped according to law and should not be regarded as bills for soliciting debts.

Guarantees and Undertakings: Guarantees and undertakings were listed as one of the 45 types in category 3 of the old regulations. The new law does not have a special item for them, but they are included in item 27 of the tax rate table, which refers to documents that guarantee the proper behavior, quality, or future of a person, item, or matter, or guarantee that a certain fact will not occur. The tax rate is still 1 jiao per item.

Pawn Tickets: The old regulations stipulated that "pawn tickets with a loan amount of 4 yuan or more" should be stamped. The new law includes pawn tickets in item 9 on loan or mortgage documents, which refers to borrowing money from someone with goods as collateral. Each item with an amount of less than 10 yuan is exempt from stamping. The Ministry of Finance has clearly instructed the Jiangsu Provincial Pawn Industry Association Federation on this interpretation (Tax Document No. 5218). The original text is published in the Compilation of Explanations of Industrial and Commercial Laws and Regulations edited by me in the eighth issue of the Commercial Monthly. However, pawn tickets were previously required to be stamped with 1 fen each. Now, at least 2 fen must be affixed to those over 10 yuan, and 4 fen must be affixed to pawn tickets worth 101 yuan. Also, loss reports are affixed with 1 jiao per item. That is, even a loss report with only 5 jiao should be affixed with 1 jiao, while a loss report with 1,000 yuan should also be affixed with only 1 jiao.

Checks: Checks used by banks and money shops, and similar instruments, were subject to progressive stamping in accordance with the old regulations, starting with 1 fen up to 1 yuan and 5 jiao. However, as a result of the request from the banking and money industry associations, the Ministry of Finance approved a postponement of stamping. This time, with the implementation of the new law, all previous cases approved by the Ministry of Finance for exemption, postponement, or reduction of stamp duty have been abolished. Checks should be stamped with 2 fen each, regardless of the amount, in accordance with item 4 of the tax rate table. Although the Shanghai Banking Association has repeatedly requested a postponement of stamping, the new tax law is a formal law passed by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government, which is not comparable to temporary regulations. It cannot be changed by administrative order. Even if there are amendments, they should go through legislative procedures. Therefore, before the Legislative Yuan officially amends it, all checks issued after September 1 should be stamped with 2 fen each according to law. The above items are the most common and should be noted during the transition between the old and new tax laws. A detailed comparison is published in the special issue on the stamp tax law in the eighth issue of the Commercial Monthly published by the City Chamber of Commerce. However, the initial edition of 5,000 copies has been sold out. The section on stamp duty is being extracted and printed separately as a special publication, which can be published around September 4. The price is 1 jiao and 5 fen per copy, plus 3 fen for postage outside the city.

Bank Association Executive Committee Discusses Stamp Tax on Checks: Temporarily Comply with Stamping During Petition Period

The Bankers Association held its 73rd Executive Committee meeting at 2 p.m. yesterday in the Association's fifth-floor conference room to discuss the stamp tax on checks. It was decided that, during the petition period, they would temporarily comply with stamping and issue an urgent notice to all bank check users. Details of the situation are recorded below. Attendees at the meeting included members of the Bankers Association, Executive Committee members, and representatives from various banks, including Wang Boyuan, Wang Zhixin, Chen Shizhen, Zhu Huisheng, Qu Jigang, Le Gengrong, Fan Jifu, Hu Xian, Huang Mohan, Chen Zheqing, Lu Zidong, Wu Weiru, Xu Xinliu, Qi Zhi, Tang Shoumin, Hu Bijiang, Yuan Mengqin, Zhu Zikui, Yao Yinpeng, Song Ziliang, Jing Runshi, Ye Fuxiao, Zhuang Zhi, Tong Ting, Xu Jilu, Wei Jinsan, Rao Taoshu, and Lin Kanghou as observer. Xu Jilu chaired the meeting.

After formal greetings, the minutes of the 72nd Executive Committee and the 68th Standing Committee meetings were read. The meeting then moved on to discuss the agenda. (1) A letter from Jiangsu Bank requesting a change of member representative was approved. (2) Regarding the issue of stamp tax on checks, it was decided that during the petition period, they would temporarily comply with stamping and publish a notice. (3) A report on the total amount of disaster relief loans underwritten by various banks and discussion of the loan agreement format. It was decided to urge the banks that have not yet confirmed to do so promptly and to review the loan agreements. (4) A letter from the Bengbu Banking Association requesting assistance regarding the Railway Department's failure to issue bills of lading for goods loaded and unloaded on dedicated sidings, which affects bank mortgage loans. It was decided to forward the matter to the Railway Department for investigation. The meeting adjourned at 4 p.m.

Urgent Notice: Yesterday, the Association issued an urgent notice to all bank check users stating: "The new Stamp Tax Law promulgated by the National Government is scheduled to take effect on September 1st. According to Article 4 of the tax rate schedule, each bank check, regardless of the amount, must be stamped with two cents. The stamping method should be carried out by the issuer (i.e., the drawer) himself when issuing the check, in accordance with the law. In order to encourage the circulation of negotiable instruments and reduce the burden on check users, the Association has repeatedly petitioned the Ministry of Finance to exempt stamping in accordance with the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Tax. As of now, the case is still under consideration. However, the implementation period of the new law is approaching soon. Most bank check users may not be familiar with the tax payment procedures, and it is inevitable that stamp omissions will occur when the law goes into effect. However, upon inspection, there is a risk of being punished according to the law, which makes it difficult for both the bank and the depositors. As the people's obligation is to abide by the government's laws, this meeting has resolved to await instructions while, during the request period, asking all bank check users to comply with stamping in accordance with the regulations in order to avoid disputes caused by violating the law. In addition to notifying the banks in attendance for their information, this notice is specially published in the newspaper to request the attention of all sectors.

Nanhua Company's Hua Wu Ship Runs Aground in Japan: Both Ship and Crew Are Insured

The Nanhua Company's Hua Wu ship was originally an Austrian ship confiscated by our Navy during the European War. It was later purchased by the Nanhua Company and continued to use the name Hua Wu. The ship is very large, with a carrying capacity of 4,249 tons. The manager is Zhao Fuchen, and the shipowner is Norwegian Johnson. Recently, the ship has been rented to others to transport coal and mineral sands between China and Japan.

Going to Japan to Unload Cargo

Last time, it was fully loaded with iron sand at Ma'anshan Island and sailed to Yokohama to unload the cargo. When leaving Pukou for Japan, it hit and damaged the towing wharf. When it arrived at Wusong, it lost an anchor. After the ship was equipped and sailed to Japan, the cargo was unloaded and prepared to return. The ship's chief mate telegraphed Zhao Fuchen, reporting that the shipowner was slightly ill and asking for instructions. Zhao replied by telegram, asking them to return to Shanghai quickly, planning to send them to Qinhuangdao to transport coal to Japan.

Encountering a Typhoon and Running Aground

The ship set sail from Yokohama and returned to Shanghai. At about 3 a.m. on the 29th, when it was about to arrive at Kobe in Mie Prefecture, Watarai County, Sukuta, and off the coast of Sumura, 50 meters away, it encountered a typhoon. There were many hidden reefs in the area, making navigation difficult. The ship ran aground there, and the hull was stranded on the reefs. The storm and rain hit fiercely, and the situation was very dangerous. Wireless and other equipment were destroyed, so they could not send an emergency message to Shanghai.

Crew Rescued

The crew members were helpless because it was late at night. It was not until dawn that they were discovered by local Japanese residents, who organized a rescue team and sent a boat to the place where the Hua Wu ran aground, rescuing some of the crew members and sailors and taking them ashore. The Shanghai company has not yet received a detailed telegram on how many people were rescued. They telegraphed Japan yesterday to inquire.

Confirmation by Telegram

Yesterday morning, reporters went to various parties to investigate the truth about the Hua Wu ship accident. Although it was already known that it had encountered misfortune, the Nanhua Company had not yet received an official telegram and still could not get accurate information. It was not until 5 p.m. that the company received a telegram from Kobe forwarded by the Japanese Daido Trading Company, stating that the Hua Wu ship had indeed encountered a typhoon and ran aground at the above-mentioned location, and the situation was very dangerous.

Only Dismantling Is Possible

The telegram was sent from Kobe at 9 a.m. yesterday and arrived in Shanghai in the afternoon. It was written in English, with only a few words, briefly stating that the Hua Wu ship ran aground very badly, and the hull had sunk into the reefs. There was no hope of rescue. Only the ship's hull can be dismantled, the telegram said. Upon receiving the news, Nanhua immediately reported it to the China Ship Insurance Joint Association and tried to investigate the loss of the ship.

Telegraphing the Consul

Based on this telegram, Zhao Fuchen first telegraphed the Chinese Consulate in Kobe in the name of the company, asking the Kobe Consulate to send someone to the scene of the Hua Wu ship accident to thoroughly investigate the loss of the ship in order to proceed with rescue operations. He also asked how many crew members were rescued and whether there were any crew members who died in the accident, and asked the Consulate to investigate and send the rescued crew members back to Shanghai.

Insurance Issues

The Hua Wu ship hull was insured with the China Ship Insurance Joint Association in this port for a total of 120,000 yuan for peace of mind insurance. All the crew members on board were also insured with the Maritime Accident Insurance Company in this port for accident insurance of 30,000 yuan. Therefore, even if the entire ship is damaged and the crew members are killed, there is compensation to be obtained. The Nanhua Company will not suffer any loss. The effectiveness of the crew's accident insurance is now seen to be very effective.

Oil Cake Merchants Oppose Guangdong's Tax Levy: Guangdong, Hankou, and Shantou Gangs Join the Strike: Manufacturers from Various Places Hold a Joint Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Countermeasures: Invite the City's News Media to Uphold Justice: Chairman Chiang's Instructions to Wait for Resolution

According to Dagong News Agency, oil cake and miscellaneous grain manufacturers from various places have repeatedly requested the abolition of Guangdong's implementation of additional import levies on bran, which is scheduled to start on September 1, but have not been approved. They have all suspended business and transportation since the day before yesterday. A joint meeting was held at 3 p.m. yesterday to discuss countermeasures and representatives were sent to the Central and Southwest authorities to petition. Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, referred the case to the Executive Yuan for review. Guangdong, Hankou, and Shantou manufacturers also suspended business yesterday. Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Miscellaneous Grain Association, hosted the news media last night to report the process. The details are as follows.

Joint Meeting of Manufacturers from Various Places

Representatives from the Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Association of this city and oil factory and cake merchants from various places held an emergency meeting at 3 p.m. yesterday on the third floor of the Miscellaneous Grain Market on Minguo Road. Gu Xinyi chaired the meeting, and Kong Rulin recorded the minutes.

Decide to Resolve the Abolition

After formal greetings, Chairman Gu Xinyi reported on the case of Guangdong's donation merchants contracting to levy bran donations. Representatives then expressed their opinions and immediately discussed (1) Guangdong Province's donation merchants are scheduled to contract to levy an additional fee of 25 cents per dan for imported bean cakes and raw cakes for the construction of Sun Yat-sen University, which is a matter of vital interest to the industry. Please discuss countermeasures. (According to the manufacturers and cake merchants' decision, the Guangdong donation merchants will implement the levy of cake donations on September 1, that is, manufacturers will stop work and cake merchants will stop transportation from that day. Please inform the factory and transportation parties to express their firm stance together in order to promote the attention of the authorities. The meeting decided to telegraph the factories in Hankou about the case, urging them to handle it uniformly in order to avoid delaying the opportunity and to send representatives to Shanghai to discuss the progress together. (2) Organize a petition group to petition the central and southwest authorities separately, requesting to stop the collection of additional donations in order to reduce the burden on farmers and avoid affecting industrial and commercial operations. It was decided to telegraph the Commander-in-Chief of the First Army Group in the Southwest, the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, the Guangdong Provincial Government, the Municipal Party Department, the Finance Commissioner's Office, the Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce, the Guangzhou Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Association, the Shantou Chamber of Commerce, the North and South Port Trade Association, the Miscellaneous Grain Association, the Central Administrative Yuan, Chairman Chiang, the Ministry of Industry, and the Ministry of Finance, making a firm statement. In addition, representatives will be sent to form a petition group to petition the central and southwest authorities separately. Wait for the Hankou representatives to arrive in Shanghai before proceeding. The meeting adjourned at 5:30 p.m.

Chairman Chiang's Instructions to Wait for Resolution

The Miscellaneous Grain Association, Guangzhao Guild Hall, Guangdong Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association, and other groups in this city jointly telegraphed Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, to strictly order the cessation of the collection of bran donations. The association received Chairman Chiang's instructions yesterday morning, stating, "A telegram has been submitted regarding the case of Guangzhou donation merchants contracting the annual salary for bran. Please forward it to the Executive Yuan for review and cancellation, and according to the original case, non-imported goods will be permanently exempted from taxation, which is in line with the recent purpose of exempting from excessive taxes and levies, and farmers and businesses will both benefit from it. The telegram has been read. Wait for the Executive Yuan to review it. Please wait for the solution." This instruction, August 29, 24th year of the Republic of China, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Seal.

Since oil cake manufacturers from Shanghai, Wuxi, Dangzhou, Kunshan, and other places have jointly suspended business and transportation since the day before yesterday, the Hankou and Guangdong and Shantou sides have also telegraphed to express their unanimous action. According to the reporter from the Dagong News Agency, after inquiring from the Zhuang companies stationed in Shanghai by various Bangs, manufacturers from Guangdong Shantou and Hankou also participated in the implementation yesterday morning, stopping transactions. Damage to the News Media Reports the Process

The Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Association hosted the news media in this city at the Xicaishe Western Restaurant on Simalu at 2 p.m. yesterday. Over sixty reporters from various newspapers attended. At the banquet, Gu Xinyi reported the Guangdong donation merchants contracting to levy donations as follows: Bean cake and peanut cake (called bean bran and cow bran in Guangdong) are inherent products of our country and are essential for farmers to fertilize their fields. Most of the products were transported and sold from the three northeastern provinces. Recently, in response to the needs of the times, manufacturers in various parts of the country have successively established factories and registered for manufacturing. There are a total of twenty factories in Shanghai, Hankou, Wuxi, Wujin, Kunshan, and other places. Tens of thousands of workers rely on it for their livelihood. The output has increased sharply, and the locks are all over the country. Guangzhou and Shantou are regarded as profitable because of the large number of sales. They secretly presented to the Finance Commissioner's Office, "Imported fertilizers still have bean bran and raw bran from Dalian and Niuzhuang and other places that have not borne donations and taxes. Please levy additional fees in the same way as imported goods, at eight dimes per dan." This is the first page of the donation merchants' attempt to indiscriminately levy domestic cake bran. Since Thailand Lishi Company secretly requested that factory cakes be imported fertilizers, attempting to indiscriminately levy additional fees, the public was outraged. The relevant industry groups in the local area argued nearby. At the same time, our association, based on the facts, telegraphed to stop it. On December 7 of the 21st year, the Finance Office's Bulletin No. 15, "Guangdong and other provinces' locally made bean bran, peanut bran, and other fertilizers are exempt from additional fees." The bright order is known to the whole country. By May of the 23rd year, the contractor, Huifeng Company, again secretly reported to the government that the raw materials for domestic bran were collected from the eastern provinces, and then the Zhongxing ship transported cake bran from Shanghai to Guangdong and was detained and donated. Our association collected the trademarks of cake bran manufactured by factories in Shanghai, Wuxi, Wu, Kun, and other places and submitted them to the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, the Guangdong Provincial Government, and the Finance Commissioner's Office to prove that Principal Zou of Sun Yat-sen University was in charge of correcting it. On that day, Principal Zou replied by telegram, "The Finance Office exempted the additional fees for bean cakes and raw bran. All those produced in the three northeastern provinces will be levied, and all those produced in the ten provinces will not be levied. The contractor has been ordered to comply with it, which is in line with the telegram." Telegrams were also successively received, stating, "The Political Affairs Committee reiterated today that no fees will be charged for bean bran that is not from the three northeastern provinces, and the levy will be reduced from eight cents to three cents." At the same time, the Shantou industry colleagues in Guangdong repeatedly petitioned the authorities, and Zhang Shaoxiong was commissioned by the Finance Office to jointly discuss the issue with Huang Peilun, a representative of Zhongda, and a representative of Huifeng Company. It was confirmed that the raw materials for domestic cake bran in various provinces were indeed not from the eastern provinces. The results of the discussion were submitted, and from then on, the bran sent to Guangdong was not produced in the three northeastern provinces and was exempt from additional fees. There are files for each case, but our association is aware that the donation merchants are greedy for money and may cause problems in the future. All the cake bran transported to Guangdong is reported by the association and issued with a certificate of approval and sent with the goods for certification. It is still handled as before. From May of last year to the present, the ink on the case has not dried up for a year, and the ashes of the levy have rekindled, and even intensified. In the past, the cake imported from the eastern provinces was levied at three cents per dan, but now it is levied at 25 cents. In the past, the cake transported from Tianjin, Qingdao, the Yangtze River, and Shanghai ports was not charged, but now it is levied at 25 cents uniformly. Recently, news was received from Guangdong that this additional fee will be implemented on September 1. It seems that this does not care about the law and does not care about the difficulties of the people. The vitality of the emerging oil factory, which is still in its infancy, will be cut off. Moreover, the Guangdong authorities are now implementing a three-year plan to abolish more than forty kinds of excessive taxes and levies because the people's power is exhausted. On the one hand, the cake bran, which is a fertilizer for farmers, is levied. How can it show credibility to the people of the country? How can the rural areas, which are on the verge of bankruptcy, bear the burden? This time, Guangdong Province implemented the levy of additional fees. All the factories, merchants, and customers in Shanghai, Hankou, Wuxi, Wu, Kun, and other places have achieved unanimous contact because they share weal and woe. It has been decided that from now on, the oil factory will stop work and the customers will stop transportation, and they will not hesitate to sacrifice everything and fight to the end. However, at present, the manufacturing companies and customers are suffering a major blow when industry and commerce are extremely declining. Unfortunately, the future can be imagined. It is hoped that everyone will express their sympathy and give enthusiastic support and publicity, so as to arouse public opinion and achieve the case that non-imported products are not subject to additional fees. It will be fortunate not only for our manufacturers, but also for the welfare of millions of farmers and workers.

We are currently rushing to protect and rescue the situation. Yesterday, I received an urgent telegram from Chairman Huang reporting that the flow of the Yellow River in Zhongmu, Henan, continues to rise to 5,500 cubic meters per second, far exceeding the capacity of the central canal to discharge. You are deeply concerned about the hunger and drowning of the people, showing utmost care. I am deeply grateful for your consideration. As a responsible official, I have a duty to console and assist, and I must appeal for relief for the disaster victims. I hope to rely on your benevolence and receive your gracious assistance. I offer my sincere thanks in advance and hope you will consider this matter. Yours sincerely, Chen Guofu, on a propitious day."

In recent times, the general phenomena in society, namely, the eight characters 'lack of etiquette, forgetfulness of righteousness, little integrity, and scarcity of shame,' are sufficient to encompass the activities of the entire population. If the people are like this, and society is like this, how can the nation and country not be poor and weak and in trouble? Although the reasons for poverty and weakness are not limited to one aspect, it is undeniable that human efforts have been lacking. Therefore, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has promoted the New Life Movement, which has been met with widespread response. The future of the country is truly dependent on this. The so-called New Life Movement, its focus is actually on self-restraint. Only by correcting oneself can one correct others. Correcting oneself and correcting others both belong to human affairs. If a reasonable adjustment can be achieved in human affairs, society will definitely not be as chaotic and dark as it is today. The National Operated Merchant Shipping Bureau's Tea Room Training Class, organized by the New Life Movement General Association, is originally a start to rectify human affairs. The intention and method are both excellent, and I will do my best to assist it, so that our maritime workers can all become healthy citizens who are polite, abide by righteousness, are honest, and know shame. I have heard that there are those outside who are opposing it for no reason, which I am not happy to hear. As for those who say that the China Merchants Bureau is using the New Life Movement training as an opportunity to actually reduce workers, I think that at a time when the unemployment problem is becoming increasingly serious, social concerns are worrying, and the China Merchants Bureau should not do this."

Special Price for Cotton Yarn and Piece Goods - Ministry Approves Extension for Another Year - Calculated from September 1st

In order to facilitate cargo merchants and promote cargo transportation, the Railway Bureau, with the approval of the Ministry of Railways, has set a special price for the transportation of cotton yarn and cotton yarn piece goods on the Beijing-Shanghai Line, reducing it by 20% according to the original grade. If transported with a certificate from the Shanghai Chinese Cotton Mill Federation, it can be reduced by another 20%. As the special price is due to expire at the end of August this year, and the transportation performance of cotton yarn and cotton yarn piece goods has improved recently, a request has been submitted to the Ministry of Railways to extend the special price for another year from September 1st. This has been approved by the Ministry Order Ye Zi No. 7320.

General Association of Marine Engineers Requests - Relief for Unemployed Seamen

The Chinese General Association of Marine Engineers, recently, because many third engineers with certificates have become unemployed, which has a significant impact on their future livelihoods. In order to find a way out for unemployed seamen and to arrange positions for third engineers, the association has held multiple meetings. It has been decided to submit a request to the Ministry to instruct various shipping companies that for ships of 2,000 tons or more, marine artisans should temporarily be replaced by third engineers. Although this is using a great talent for a small job, it is also unavoidable. The submission is as follows: "Submitting a request to provide relief to third engineers to find a way out and avoid unemployment: Recently, members Lin Xiebin and others submitted a report stating that although members have passed the examination in accordance with the Ministry-promulgated Seafarer Examination Regulations and have obtained Class B third engineer certificates issued by the Ministry, they are still unable to find work and have been unemployed for a long time, which is painful to express. I implore the association to forward this to the Ministry for prompt relief in order to maintain their livelihoods, etc. Upon investigation, the matters stated by the members are indeed the actual situation. However, according to the Ministry's regulations, third engineers may only be employed on ships over 3,000 tons. However, the number of seafarers continuing to apply for third engineer certificates is endless, increasing without end, resulting in an oversupply. Looking ahead, I am deeply concerned. Under this deformed state, how will these third engineers be arranged? Moreover, the third engineer is the lowest rank among marine engineers, and it is even more difficult to provide relief for the unemployment problem than for other seafarers. If they are to serve beyond their rank, it is not permitted by law. If they are to change careers midway, it is difficult to bear from a human perspective. Even if they are to accept a lower rank and become marine artisans, according to Article 35, Section 2 of the Seafarer Examination Regulations, there is no hope of promotion for life. The association has repeatedly considered this and feels that it is difficult to advance or retreat, which has a significant impact on the future livelihoods of seafarers. Moreover, marine artisans are already abundant, and it is not easy to find a place. Even if there are vacancies, why must third engineers with certificates be hired? From this point of view, the third engineer certificate is like an unfulfilled check, with minimal utility, like waste paper, which was not anticipated by the Ministry when it initially drafted the law. However, although the problem is small, it is closely related to the credibility of the Ministry's laws and regulations. If relief is not sought urgently, not only will this local unemployment problem inevitably become more serious, but it will also overflow and collapse, and a small spark will start a prairie fire, which may be difficult to contain once it is triggered. The implications will cause the value of certificates to be negatively affected everywhere. The association believes that the matter concerns the livelihoods of seafarers and should not be ignored, and that it also has a great obstacle to the promotion of the entire shipping industry. After repeated consideration, I can only implore the Ministry to promptly investigate how many existing ships in China's rivers and seas are over 3,000 tons, and how many third engineers have received certificates over the years, and compare them with each other to understand clearly. If there is indeed an oversupply, there should be a comprehensive planning strategy for this situation of too few portions for too many monks. I propose to the Ministry to change the method and issue a clear order to all shipping companies in the country that for ships of 2,000 tons or more that only use marine artisans and do not have third engineers, the marine artisan positions should be uniformly replaced by third engineers, and the salary should still be paid as a marine artisan. However, there is priority in hiring. Only when the number of third engineers is not enough to distribute can marine artisans be used instead. This fundamental solution is also a necessary measure to provide relief to seafarers. Although it is known to be contrary to the Ministry's regulations, it can promote safety in Hangzhou transportation, and shipowners can also obtain technical assistance. It can not only seek a way out for seafarers, but also add a guarantee to the Ministry's certificates, achieving multiple benefits in one stroke. I respectfully submit my humble opinion and await adoption. Is this appropriate? I respectfully request a prompt order for implementation, without allowing for any hesitation. I respectfully submit to Zhu, Minister of Transportation."

Private Drug-Making Operation Uncovered in Taoyuanfang After Someone Jumps from Building - Reason for Luo Zhaoxiu's Jump Still Under Investigation - 26 Types of Red Pill-Making Equipment Seized

At approximately 5 a.m. the other morning, a person suddenly jumped from the carpentry workshop on the upper floor of No. 165 Taoyuanfang, North Jiangxi Road, injuring their buttocks. Tang Fuxiang, an apprentice in the workshop, saw this and reported it to the Chinese Constable on duty at post No. 1894. An ambulance was summoned and the person was sent to Tongren Hospital. It was learned that the person was named Luo Zhaoxiu, also known as A'er, from Taizhou. When asked why this happened, the person refused to say. The person was admitted to the hospital for treatment. Later, the second landlord, Zhu Mao, learned of this and went to investigate. Seeing that the room door was closed, he knew that there were illegal items inside, so he and Chinese Constables No. 1283 and others went upstairs, opened the door, and seized a handbag containing up to 26 kinds of equipment for making the drug "red pills," as well as tens of thousands of drug pills. They telegraphed the Hongkou Police Station, which sent Chinese and foreign detectives to rush to the scene. They continued to seize a Hangzhou woman named Pang Li, who had rented a room in the alley. After waiting for a while, a Cantonese man named Yang Renchu arrived and was also arrested. Together with the evidence, they were all taken to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, the three men and women, including the Luo criminal, who had recovered in the hospital, were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Wang Yaotang of the Shanghai Municipal Council detailed the previous circumstances and stated that the identity of the boss of the operation had not been determined and requested an extension of time. Subsequently, the detectives reported the details of the investigation and presented the evidence. The second landlord, Zhu Mao, a local, stated that he ran a machine factory at No. 155 Qipu Road. The ground floor of the premises was sublet to a carpentry workshop, and the room upstairs was rented from him by the defendant Pang Li at the end of last year for a monthly rent of 25 yuan, which was collected by the accountant Yang Zhaoxian. He did not know that she was secretly making red pills upstairs. According to Yang, he went to collect the rent every month, and the door was closed. He had to knock on the door to notify her, and Pang Li would pay the rent. The rental agreement was in the name of Liu Haiqing. According to apprentice Tang Fuxiang, he was cooking breakfast at the time when he suddenly saw the defendant Luo Zhaoxiu jump from the upper floor and fall to the ground. He did not know what had happened and immediately reported it to the Chinese Constables. When questioned, the defendants' statements were evasive. Judge Jiang Shuzi ordered that they be returned to custody separately and rescheduled for investigation and verification.

New Life Movement Youth Service Corps - Continues to Rectify City Appearance - Starting Next Month

The Youth Service Corps of the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association will conclude its fourth, fifth, and sixth phases of service, guidance, and inspection of the cleanliness of various restaurants, hotels, and barbershops at the end of this month. Starting next month, it will continue its work of rectifying the appearance of the city, with a focus on guiding residents in neighborhoods. The seventh phase of service key points has been issued to various sub-corps and informed to the team leaders and members, and posted in various neighborhoods. It is scheduled to be implemented starting September 1 (i.e., this Sunday). The key points are extracted below:

Key Points of the Seventh Phase of Service of the Youth Service Corps

Item: Rectify the appearance of the city (neighborhoods and households)

Goal: Cleanliness and order

Standards:

(1) The names of neighborhoods and the door numbers within the neighborhoods are clear and easy to recognize.

(2) The entrances of neighborhoods are kept clean and tidy, signs are not hung randomly, and iron gates should be installed and people assigned to take care of them.

(3) A designated posting area should be set up at the entrance of the neighborhood to prevent random posting of rental papers, etc.

(4) The walkways inside the neighborhoods are clean, streetlights are sufficient, and ditches are unobstructed.

(5) Public urinals and trash cans are set up, and efforts are made to prevent the breeding of filth.

(6) Residents do not pile up miscellaneous items in front of their doors, paying special attention to cleanliness.

(7) No wireless radios or other noises are allowed before 6 a.m. or after 12 p.m.

(8) At any time prevent crowds from quarreling, use your strength to pay attention to the public quiet of the residents in the neighborhoods.

Supplementary rules:

Conveniently pay attention to whether the following matters are good or not:

(1) Pedestrians must follow the pedestrian standards.

(2) It is forbidden to set up altars for religious rituals or other superstitious activities in the neighborhood.

(3) Heavy vehicles are prevented from entering.

(4) Residents are advised to stop drying clothes across the street.

Notes:

(1) Those that do not meet these standards should be persuaded to correct them one by one, according to their nature, to the neighborhood head, the lease office, the watchmen, and the residents. If there is an unreasonable refusal, the police can be notified nearby to reprimand them and record their names.

(2) The above-mentioned service situation and opinions of each service should be reported by the team leader and sent to the sub-corps leader for submission to the corps headquarters.

French Concession Lumber Industry Hygiene Donation - Forced to Endure the Pain of Donating

The New News Agency reports that various lumber businesses in the French Concession of this city were suddenly notified by the French Municipal Council to obtain classified business hygiene licenses and pay an inspection fee of 2 yuan or 10 yuan. The businesses, having been in operation for many years and never having paid such a donation, found the content of the donation harsh and difficult to accept, and therefore unanimously opposed it. They had written to the trade association to forward a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce requesting the municipal government to stop it, and had also written to the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association requesting the French authorities to abolish it. It is now learned that detectives from the French Police Station suddenly sent letters to various lumber firms, such as Tongxing, Chengda, Fuxing, and Lida, to go to the French Police Station for questioning. The foreign detective chief advised the lumber firms to donate for the licenses. The lumber firms replied with reason, but to no avail. The foreign detective chief then sent police to take the firms to the Municipal Council to donate for the licenses. The firms, forced by the circumstances, had no choice but to endure the pain of donating for the licenses. It is said that the lumber firms will report the situation of this forced donation to various agencies and groups to request assistance.

Vicious Daughter-in-Law Beats Mother-in-Law - Taken to District Court for Interrogation

Yang Zhang, a woman from Chengjiaqiao Dajin Township in the Pusong District, is nearing sixty years of age. Because she had no son, she adopted her nephew, Fuyi, as her son in the past. Two years ago, for Fuyi she married a woman with the surname Gao, Gao. At the beginning of her marriage, Gao was considered filial. Yang Zhang was pleased and thought that she was about to die, so she took out all the property deeds, such as land deeds and house deeds, and handed them over to Gao for safekeeping, entrusting all family affairs to her daughter-in-law. Unexpectedly, after Gao took over, she suddenly changed her behavior. She treated her mother-in-law like a servant on weekdays, scolding indirectly and making the family restless. Yang Zhang, because of an urgent need, asked her daughter-in-law Gao to take out a land deed in order to mortgage it for some money. Unexpectedly, Gao slapped her in the face, tore her lip, and caused her to bleed profusely, shouting for help. Neighbors gathered and learned the situation. The crowd felt injustice on her behalf and reported it to the Chengjiaqiao Police Station. The inspector, Zhu Dingzhang, sent police to arrest Yang Gao. According to Yang Zhang's confession of being beaten, Gao's denial was absurd. Yang Zhang was ordered to return to her home for treatment, while a document was prepared to send Yang Gao to the Public Security Bureau, who transferred her to the District Court for interrogation and legal action yesterday.

Jiangbei Bandit Leader - Jie Pengfei Approved for Transfer - Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters Submitted Official Document - Bandit Has Gunshot Scar on Right Leg

Jie Pengfei, also known as Jie Wu and Lian Sheng, a Jiangbei bandit from Moyang, is forty-one years old this year. He repeatedly committed major cases of banditry, kidnapping, arson, and murder in the territory of Haizhou Donghai County. The Donghai County Government offered a reward for his arrest. Because Jie could not stand in the Jiangbei area, he fled to Shanghai. The Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters received a confidential report from informants, learning that Jie was hiding at No. 70, Qian Tan Residence, Xinxiao West, Nanshi, Huajie. Therefore, they sent Cai Zhaofeng, director of the special affairs team, along with special affairs officers Shao Shike, service officer Shao Hanzhang, to Shanghai, and Shanghai Public Security Bureau detectives to arrest him. Jie had heard the news and moved away. After investigation, it was learned that Jie had moved to No. 310, Avenue LaFayette, in the French Concession. Therefore, on the afternoon of the 27th, they reported to the French Police Station and requested them to send detectives Lu Zhulin and Bao Detective Liu Jinrong to rush to the address to arrest Jie. He was taken back to the police station. The next day, Jie was escorted to the Second Special Court, where Judge Wang Gangxu opened a hearing. Jie denied being a thief, and the Police Department opposed the transfer because the Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters had not provided evidence. The court ruled to detain him pending investigation and verification. The details were recorded in the previous report. Currently, the police station has sent detectives to investigate and confirmed that Jie did live in the Dan Residence in Xinxiaotou. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang of the Second Special Court came to the First Criminal Court to continue the interrogation. He questioned Jie again, and Jie still denied being a thief, saying that he had three brothers and was not called Jie Wu. Then, Jie's concubine, Ms. Huang (29 years old, from Jiangbei), was summoned to court and testified that they had lived at No. 70 Tan Residence. The Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters also presented the Donghai County Government's wanted notice and telegram to the court. French Police Station Detective Lu Zhulin reported that Jie's right leg had a gunshot scar. After the court reviewed the evidence, it ruled that Jie Pengfei, also known as Jie Wu, was approved to be handed over to the Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters personnel for interrogation.

Hongxing Bank Illegally Sells Inferior Silver Coins; Over Two Thousand Nine Hundred "Double Corner" Coins Confiscated; Bank Supervisor Ye Lifu Arrested

Detective Wang Jiaju and Detective Bao Dezhong of the Old Zhabei Police Station received information that someone was using inferior silver coins at Dafazhan, located at No. 54 on West Guangdong Road. They reported this to Chief Detective You A'gen. At 1:50 PM the day before yesterday, they went to the premises and arrested Yao Shusheng, a local man. They confiscated twenty inferior "double corner" coins and took him to the police station. Yao confessed that he had purchased the counterfeit coins from Hongxing Bank at No. 110 North Hai Road. He could exchange one silver dollar for 13 to 15 "double corner" coins, but he had to use the code "Guang San" to make the purchase. The detectives then used two marked banknotes, escorted Yao to the bank, and successfully purchased thirty inferior "double corner" coins. The detectives then searched the premises and found 2,985 such "double corner" coins upstairs. They took the bank employees Gu Yungeng, Jin Bingkun, Lu Shirong, Lu Bohua, and Xu Chengshi to the police station. Subsequently, they arrested Ye Li, the bank supervisor, on Guizhou Road near Beijing Road. However, the manager, Shen Guolian, had gone to Nanxiang and was not arrested. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Special District Court's Criminal Division One. The police lawyer Jiang Baoqing explained the situation and requested an extension, stating that the police needed to continue their investigation. Subsequently, the detective in charge of the case submitted a report detailing the circumstances of the arrest and stating that the counterfeit coins had been examined by employees of a certain bank at No. 119 Guizhou Road, who said that the "double corner" coins were not generally accepted in the market. The court reviewed the case, briefly questioned the defendants, and ordered a one-week postponement for further questioning.

Robbery on Route Doumer; Bandit Shoots Victim

Shen Mulin, a 37-year-old local resident living at No. 22, Lane 133 on Route Doumer in the French Concession, was hardworking and frugal, and his family was well-off, which attracted the attention of robbers. At about 9 o'clock last night, four strangers suddenly broke into his house, claiming to be asking for directions. They lingered and refused to leave. Shen happened to be home and, realizing that they were not good people, shouted for robbers. The thugs panicked, fearing the police would arrive, and quickly walked out. However, one of the robbers at the rear, unable to control his anger, turned around and fired two warning shots. One shot missed, but the other hit Shen's left arm, with the bullet passing through. As the stray bullet flew, it grazed the head of his relative, Zhang (72 years old), causing only a minor injury. After the robbers fled, they reported the incident to the Lujiawan Police Station, which sent detectives to investigate. Shen was then taken by car to Guangru Hospital for treatment.

Jardine Matheson's "Desheng" Ship; Yesterday Hosted Visitors from All Sectors; The Ship's Equipment is Excellent and Speed Has Increased; Maiden Voyage to Qingdao from Shanghai This Morning

The new "Desheng" ship of Jardine Matheson Steam Navigation Company, after arriving in Shanghai from England, was docked at Jardine Matheson Wharf on Broadway Road in Hongkou. Yesterday, from 2 PM to 4 PM, it hosted visitors from all sectors. The equipment is fully equipped and the maiden voyage to Qingdao from Shanghai will be this morning. Details are as follows:

Fully Equipped: A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency boarded the ship yesterday for a tour and was personally hosted by the compradore Chen Langshan. The ship's total tonnage is 4,376 tons, and the speed is 16 nautical miles per hour. All arrangements are very complete. There are fifteen first-class cabins, each with two beds, for a total of 30 passengers. There are fourteen second-class cabins, each with two beds, for a total of 28 passengers. There are twenty-eight third-class berths, for a total of 28 passengers. The fourth-class common cabin can accommodate about 500 passengers. The first-class and second-class dining rooms are luxuriously decorated and the cabins are comfortable and clean. A special feature is that the cargo hoists use motors, so there is no noise when lifting, which does not disturb passengers. The anti-theft equipment is thorough, and the bridge is equipped with an automatic alarm. Each cabin has instructions on how to wear life jackets, and there are six lifeboats. Life rafts and life jackets are fully equipped. Third and fourth-class cabins are equipped with flush toilets, bathtubs, and washbasins. Five British escort soldiers are assigned to prevent any incidents.

Shortened Time: The captain is (Pettigrew) and there are eight officers: the first mate, second mate, third mate, fourth mate, chief engineer, first engineer, and second engineer, all of whom are British. There is one radio operator. There are twenty-seven sailors and twenty-seven stokers, all of whom are Chinese. The compradore's staff consists of forty-five people, including fourteen service personnel, and the rest are accountants and cooks. All service personnel are trained and qualified. Tips are not required. The journey from Shanghai to Qingdao takes 24 hours, from Shanghai to Shantou it takes 46 hours, from Shantou to Hong Kong it takes 12 hours, and from Hong Kong to Guangzhou it takes 6 hours, which is faster than other ships.

Sailing to Qing: The Desheng ship is scheduled to depart on its maiden voyage from Jardine Matheson Wharf in Shanghai to Qingdao at 11 AM today, and is expected to arrive at around 11 AM tomorrow, immediately hosting people from all sectors in Qingdao to board the ship for a tour. The compradore Chen Liangshan and the second compradore Xu Heqing will both accompany to host the event. It is decided that the ship will return from Qingdao to Shanghai on the 4th and arrive on the 5th. The company will then host people from all sectors to tour the ship, and will schedule voyages from Shanghai to Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou.

Ticket Prices: The ticket prices for the Desheng ship are as follows: (1) From Shanghai to Shantou, first class is 23 yuan, second class is 20 yuan, third class is 10 yuan, and fourth class is 5 yuan. To Hong Kong, first class is 23 yuan, second class is 20 yuan, third class is 11 yuan, and fourth class is 6 yuan. To Guangzhou, first class is 25 yuan, second class is 22 yuan, third class is 12 yuan, and fourth class is 6.5 yuan. (2) From Shanghai to Qingdao, first class is 16 yuan, second class is 14 yuan, third class is 7 yuan, and fourth class is 3 yuan. The route is Qingdao, Shanghai, Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou.

The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway received instructions from the Ministry of Railways yesterday, stating that in order to expand the Hepingmen Station, it is planned to first acquire more than two mu of triangular land in front of the station building to build roads and parking lots. Ye Zhongfang's Nature Hard to Change; Beats a Guard in Prison; Dissatisfied with Eating Soybeans, Ye Actually Assaults the Guard

Ye Zhongfang, grandson of the late Ningbo Zhenhai native Ji Chengzhong, nicknamed "Little Shaker," was sued for divorce by his wife, Chen Yinglan, in the Second Special District Court. After three trials, the court ruled in favor of the divorce and ordered Ye to pay 60,000 yuan in alimony. The Second Special District Court enforced the judgment in accordance with the law. Because Ye refused to appear in court, the court sent officials to detain Ye in June and enforce the judgment, and he has been detained for more than two months. Because all of his property has been exhausted, he has not paid a single penny. Ye is detained in Room 3 of the civil detention department of the Second Special District Court's detention center. His addictions have been quit. His concubine, Lu Xiaomei, a local, brings food and delicacies to the detention center every morning to visit him. Therefore, Ye is more spirited than before and is content. He sits at the south window, writing articles, which he occasionally sends to small newspapers for publication. However, his shaking nature has not changed in detention. Yesterday morning at about 7 AM, he suddenly started shaking violently in the detention center because he was dissatisfied with the soybeans that Zhejiang native Shi Zemin, a guard, distributed with the congee, which led to a verbal dispute. Ye actually punched Shi in the right cheek, causing Shi's eyelid to be scratched by his fingers. After the guards stopped him, Shi immediately reported the incident to the warden, who investigated and ordered Ye to be sent to the Second Special District Court's Procuratorate for investigation. At noon, Prosecutor Wang Ren and Clerk Zhao Yifen took their seats in Criminal Division Five and ordered Ye Zhongfang to be brought to the court for investigation. Ye was wearing a blue cloth long gown, was bald and barefoot, wearing slippers, with glasses on his nose and a short mustache on his upper lip. He had a plaster on his left cheek and looked exhausted. Presumably, he has been ill in detention recently. His concubine, Lu Xiaomei, who had come to the detention center in the morning to visit him, heard the news and waited, and she also came to the court to listen quietly. The court first interrogated Ye Zhongfang, 27 years old, from Zhenhai, who used to study and lived at No. 22, Lane 269, Carter Road, and is now unemployed. He is being detained in the detention center for an alimony case related to his divorce. Then, the official summoned the plaintiff Shi Zemin to testify, 49 years old, from Zhejiang, who is a guard at the detention center, living inside. Today morning at about 7 AM, I went upstairs to distribute congee. Ye was standing at the door of Room 3, complaining that the soybeans were too hard and he couldn't eat them. He wanted me to change them for tender ones. I replied that they were all the same. He immediately punched me in the face, causing my eyelid to be scratched by his fingers. The guards pulled him away. He then used a broom to hit my right shoulder and behind my shoulder once each. I have no grievances with him. However, he usually asks me to buy cigarettes, which I have not allowed. The official asked if Ye denied the assault. Ye denied the assault, stating that Shi and another detainee, Guo Yongji, were arguing about soybeans, and I went to dissuade them. I have had a fever for six days and was sleeping in bed. How could I hit anyone? Besides, I don't eat soybeans, so what does it matter to me if they are hard or tender? The plaintiff Shi Zemin denied arguing with the person named Guo and stated that Ye loses his temper in the detention center, and even if the dishes sent from home are not to his liking. Of course, he won't eat soybeans. He deliberately makes trouble for the authorities. Prosecutor Wang verified the testimonies and ordered Shi Zemin to go to the Forensic Medical Office to examine the injuries. Ye Shenfang was returned to custody to await further verification and then adjourned the court.

Labor Representatives from Two Railways Petitioned Yesterday to Be Exempted from Physical Examinations; Director Huang Explained that There Was Absolutely No Intention to Eliminate Workers

Following the release of a notice by the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau announcing periodic physical examinations for employees, rumors immediately spread among all railway workers, causing widespread panic and unease. For days, workers have been requesting meetings of various branch unions to discuss relief measures. On the 29th, representatives from the Nanjing branch, Changzhou branch, Upper North branch, and Upper South branch of the railway union petitioned the management bureau. Director Huang personally met with the representatives and explained the meaning of the physical examinations in detail. He vehemently stated that there was absolutely no intention to eliminate workers and urged all workers to continue working with peace of mind. The representatives returned to their respective branches to relay the message to the workers, but they all considered it empty talk and felt that there was no guarantee. They have now unanimously decided to proceed based on the reasons presented to the Party headquarters and the Labor and Sanitation Department of the two railways: (1) When workers joined the railways, they had already undergone thorough medical examinations before being hired. They work hard for eight or nine hours every day and have served for decades, enduring the harshness of the weather. It is natural for the strong to become weak and the young to become old. Moreover, workers must undergo rigorous examinations every time they are promoted, and even slight deficiencies result in disqualification. (2) The workers' health has deteriorated due to their service. The bureau should show extra compassion, rather than resorting to suspension. Although some may be old and frail, they do not make mistakes in their work and should be supported. (3) The two railways have suffered repeatedly from warfare, especially during the sudden outbreak of the January 28th Incident. Workers risked their lives under gunfire to maintain railway property, saving countless assets. Within days of the signing of the ceasefire agreement, full traffic was restored, demonstrating the workers' diligent service. The bureau should consider this and continue to exempt them from examinations to ensure their security.

Recent News from the Jiangwan Teng Peifu Kindergarten

The Jiangwan Teng Peifu Kindergarten is one of the most successful emerging institutions of its kind in Shanghai. It was founded last summer and is managed by Mrs. Guo Bingwen and Ms. Sang Wenlan. The kindergarten is located on Teng Pei Road in Jiangwan, across from the Shanghai Animal Husbandry Milk Company, in an open area with fresh air. The kindergarten building was specifically designed for childcare purposes, featuring an elegant building divided into children's classrooms, playrooms, dining halls, bedrooms, bathrooms, washrooms, nanny rooms, offices, and staff rooms, all well-equipped, clean, and beautiful. The grounds are covered with grass, planted with flowers and trees, and equipped with various play and exercise equipment. The kindergarten is divided into two sections: a kindergarten section for children aged four to five, and a primary school section for children aged six to ten. The organizational structure includes Mrs. Guo as the principal, Ms. Sang as the vice-principal, Ms. Cao as a teacher, and two nannies. The kindergarten's main achievements are in health, care, and life management. Ms. Sang is the full-time person in charge. Since the Guangli era (early years of the Republic), she has served in education in Hangzhou, Nanjing, Beijing, Shanghai, and Yunnan, known for her competence, diligence, kindness, and consideration. Therefore, everything in the kindergarten is well-organized, and she treats other people's children as her own, with extensive experience in childcare and medicine. As a result, the twenty or so children entrusted to the kindergarten in the past year have all been healthy, plump, clean, and lively, earning the trust of their parents. When the kindergarten was founded, it originally had a charitable nature, intending to accommodate children orphaned after the January 28th Incident and years of flooding. However, because almost all those admitted were children of intellectuals, the nature of the kindergarten was changed to meet the needs of couples who both work and are unable to care for their children. Currently, the kindergarten charges 54 yuan per student per semester, including tuition, board, lodging, and miscellaneous expenses. By Shanghai standards, this barely covers expenses. However, thanks to Mrs. Guo Bingwen's efforts in fundraising, the kindergarten spent 2,000 yuan in start-up costs and 1,500 yuan in recurring expenses last year, in addition to the 11,500 yuan spent on the building. Therefore, the kindergarten differs in nature from general commercial schools in Shanghai and is entirely dedicated to social service. Last year, as a trial, it only admitted twenty children. This year, due to the successful trial, it plans to expand to thirty students, with ten vacancies remaining. If gentlemen and ladies have children in need, they can contact the kindergarten. Children in the Jiangwan city center area can also attend as day students. The kindergarten is now in session and welcomes visits and guidance from early childhood education experts and the public. At the beginning of this children's year, the kindergarten's contribution is well worth the reference and study of educators.

Minutes of the Meeting of the Drivers' Mutual Aid Society of the British-Owned Public Bus Company

The Drivers' Mutual Aid Society of the British-Owned China Public Bus Company held its second joint meeting of directors and supervisors at the association's office at 11:30 PM the night before. More than 30 people attended, and Sha Youqing was publicly elected as chairman, with Jiang Xiangjun as the recorder. After the formalities, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting and the status of the association's affairs, as well as the misunderstanding between the old and new directors and supervisors and the reconciliation process. Then, they began discussing important resolutions, as listed below: (1) Regarding how to handle members who are overdue in paying their membership dues: Resolution: All members who do not pay their dues within the three-month period from August 7th to October 10th of this year will be treated as new members according to the regulations. (2) Regarding how to preserve the membership dues paid by members during the first term (March 1, 1933 to July 31, 1935): Resolution: All membership dues paid by members during the first term will be permanently preserved. However, if the member withdraws from the association in the future and owes four jiao in regular fees, but does not owe membership dues, this exception does not apply. (3) Regarding whether to issue bus passes to members who owe membership dues: Resolution: This will be discussed later. (4) Regarding how to handle the membership dues previously paid by foremen: Resolution: The association will keep them on their behalf and return them in full when they legally leave their positions. The meeting adjourned with refreshments late at 1 AM.

Jingwu Society Travels to Yandang Mountain

Yandang Mountain is a major scenic spot in eastern Zhejiang. Recently, due to convenient transportation, more and more people have been visiting. The Shanghai Jingwu Sports Association's Travel Department has organized a Yandang Mountain tour group, taking the Hangzhou-Wenzhou Highway, passing famous scenic spots and historical sites along the way, such as Fangyan, Lingyan in Yongkang, Xiandu, Dinghu in Jinyun, Shimen Cave, Gushan in Lishui, Sanyan Temple in Qingtian, and Jiangxin Temple in Wenzhou. The tour travels by private car, with flexible stops. The return trip will be by sea to Shanghai, lasting eleven days, with a journey of over 700 kilometers, alternating between boats and cars to ensure a comfortable trip for the tourists. The departure date is September 14th (Saturday) at 3:15 PM on the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train, arriving at Yandang Mountain on September 18th. On September 23rd, they will take a boat from Wenzhou back to Shanghai, arriving at the port at 5 AM on September 25th. The cost is 62 yuan, including boat, car, board, and lodging (third-class seats on the Shanghai-Hangzhou train, second-class seats on the Hangzhou-Jiang train, and first-class cabins on the ship). The quota is 20 people. Registration starts immediately and closes on September 8th. It is said that half of the quota has already been filled.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather around Shandong is cloudy, with variable winds. The Yangtze River basin has northeast winds and localized showers. The East China Sea has mild cyclones and rain, caused by a low-pressure system moving northeast. The weather around Taiwan is cloudy, with northwest to southwest winds of varying strengths. The center of the hurricane was within about 60 miles of 45 degrees north latitude and 146 degrees east longitude at 2 PM, moving northeast with strong winds. Also, the highest temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday was 89.1 degrees, and the lowest was 70.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 85.1 degrees, and the lowest was 73.2 degrees.

Letters to the Editor

Having recently read today's (30th) newspapers, I was astonished by the new column stating that Cai Langsheng, the leader of the defense corps, tied up Zhuang Dingyou and dragged him to the nearby Chenjia Ancestral Hall (the site of the former defense post), where he was subjected to private torture by hanging, witnessed by the police officer of the Longhua sub-station. Most of the story about releasing Zhuang Dingyou is fabricated to mislead the public. After investigation, it was found that the patrol officer Liu Songjian sent a senior policeman to the scene. While walking to the Longhua Railway Station, about a li away from the Chenjia Ancestral Hall, he met Cai Langsheng and a member of the corps, Chen Mingxin, who were about to take a group of offenders to the corps for questioning. Unexpectedly, the senior policeman and others, without asking the reason, forcibly stopped the offenders. Cai Langsheng argued that the procedure required the corps to question them first and then transfer them to the sub-station with a written document. Therefore, he argued reasonably, leading to a quarrel. The senior policeman and others, relying on their numbers, immediately punched and kicked Cai Langsheng and Chen Mingxin, the member of the corps, in front of many witnesses, including shopkeepers. After the beating, the policeman threw the leader and the corps members into the sub-station as well. As for tying up Zhuang Dingyou with rope, that was indeed the case. Because the offender Zhuang Dingyou was strong and carried a small knife about six inches long, the rope was used to prevent him from using the knife to commit violence, which is a necessary precaution when capturing offenders and not illegal. As for private torture by hanging, it is entirely fabricated. The defense corps handles civil disputes to assist the police where their strength is insufficient. If they can be resolved through reconciliation, they are resolved. Otherwise, they are transferred to the nearest public security bureau for handling. They have never used torture on offenders. This is a fact of the past, well known to local people. Furthermore, the story that twelve jiao were taken from Zhuang Dingyou is even more ridiculous. Although the members of the defense corps are volunteers, they all have legitimate occupations and do not make a living by robbery. There is no need to dwell on this. The matter concerns the reputation of the entire defense corps. In addition to making further representations, I am writing to request that you disclose the truth and correct the report. Sincerely, The First Team of the Caojing District Defense Corps of Shanghai, August 30.

Dear Editor, The news item in your newspaper on the 27th of this month, "Social Bureau Bans Illegal Fee Collection by Cooked Water Guild," contains some misunderstandings. I am writing to explain the situation and respectfully request that your newspaper uphold justice and correct the report to avoid serious damage to the reputation of our guild. Our guild's expenses are not paid because so many membership fees are owed, and it doesn't have the funds to send water ladles. So, the executive committee meeting resolved to collect six jiao for the cost of the water ladle and two jiao for the membership certificate, which was submitted to the Social Bureau for record. In early August, it was implemented and delivered, and soon the guild complied with the Social Bureau's order to change it and not charge any fees for the water ladle. Instead, it collected two yuan in membership fees to maintain the society. It has debts more than a year old, and can't avoid collecting that money. It happened that a rogue in Nanshi fabricated charges, and our guild has already filed a lawsuit with the court to investigate and prosecute it. In short, our guild has not violated any laws. The facts are all there. I respectfully wish your editor peace. Sincerely, Shanghai Cooked Water Shop Industry Guild.

Dear Editor, Having recently read the news item in your newspaper on the 30th of this month, "The Turmoil of Huafeng's Dismissal Dispute: Worker Dies after Being Seriously Injured, Lawsuit Entrusts Lawyer to Accuse Ye Shantao of Masterminding the Incident," that the worker Yao Tianfu died of exposure for two nights and beatings yesterday morning, after investigation, it was found that the deceased Yao Tianfu was from Haining and lived in the factory. He suffered from carbuncles and had been dead for several days, as evidenced by the prescription of Doctor Dang Jingbo. After the death of the patient, his brother-in-law Zhu collected the body and put it in the Haichang Public Office. The facts are all there and have nothing to do with the labor dispute. The report in your newspaper that I, Ye Shantao, masterminded the injury and death is inconsistent with the facts. In order to clarify the truth, I am writing to request that your newspaper disclose the truth and correct the report. Sincerely, Ye Shantao, August 30. Kun Yi's business is in Shanghai, and he is accustomed to leaving early and returning late. He has been running along the Shanghai-Nanjing Road for decades, and he has been taught several lessons by pickpockets and thieves. But being framed for profit is a new experience. A few days ago, when I returned to my hometown from Shanghai, I found a package of opium ash, weighing about three qian, in my pocket. I was surprised and wondered where this thing came from. After thinking carefully, I realized that when I was taking the No. 5 tram on Nanjing Road, a group of three people bought tickets and called for the North Station. Perhaps at this time, someone took the opportunity to plant it on me, so that when we got off at the North Station, they could report to the police and get a reward for providing information. Fortunately, we sat in a car and did not enter the North Station. Otherwise, I would have been unjustly accused and become a fish in the net. The world is dangerous, and people are sinister. False accusations and extortion are emerging endlessly. Therefore, I am writing to inform travelers to be vigilant. If your editor can publish this in the newspaper, it will be a great merit. Sincerely, Gu Kunyi.
