Education News

National Free Education Association to Hold a Meeting Today to Discuss Six Items

(Nanjing, 30th) The National Free Education Committee will hold a meeting at the Ministry of Education on the morning of the 31st. The six items to be discussed are: 1. Electing three standing committee members; 2. Experimenting with short-term elementary school curriculum standards and textbooks; 3. Methods for dividing elementary school districts in various provinces and cities; 4. Methods for investigating school-age children; 5. Methods for rewarding and punishing county magistrates for promoting free education; 6. Free education inspection issues.

Ministry of Education Instructs Improvement of Public and Private Universities in Sichuan

The Ministry of Education issued an instruction on the 30th to public and private universities in Sichuan to earnestly improve, with the text as follows:

(1) Instruction to National Sichuan University, briefly stating: "The Ministry has previously sent personnel to inspect the school. According to the submitted report, after further review, in addition to the changes in the organization of departments and the abolition of affiliated schools, which were previously instructed by telegram, the main points are now presented as follows. You are to comply with them and earnestly improve, and submit a report for review and approval. 1. The organization of the school's departments should be reorganized according to the following points: (1) The departments of the College of Liberal Arts should be handled according to the current situation. After the Chongqing University College of Liberal Arts students have been identified and approved, they should be merged into the college. However, after checking, the Education Department's second-year class has only one student, who should be instructed to transfer to another department or find a way to transfer schools. (2) The Department of Physics and the Department of Mathematics in the College of Science have few students. The school should decide whether to merge them into a Department of Mathematics and Physics and must quickly seek to enrich the teaching staff and equipment. (3) The classes of the Department of Political Science and the Department of Economics in the College of Law are incomplete. If the number of students in the original classes is too small, they should be merged into a Department of Political Science and Economics. (4) The addition of the College of Agriculture, temporarily set up one or two departments. The details are to be determined by the school and reported to the Ministry for approval. After the students of the Provincial Agricultural College and the students of the Department of Agronomy and Chemistry of Chongqing University have been identified and approved, they should be merged into the college. Those who have no classes to enter may adopt borrowing or other appropriate methods. The college should do its best to enrich itself this year and temporarily determine enrollment. 2. The school's funding should be properly allocated to determine the proportion of each college. As for the purchase costs, the proportion occupied in the past was too small, resulting in simple equipment. In the future, efforts should be made to increase the amount to no less than 15% of the total funding, to be used as much as possible to expand equipment, and the College of Agriculture should pay special attention to enrichment. 3. The school's courses are mostly set up for individuals, without a fixed standard. The teaching materials used are estimated to be more than 150 types, costing 30,000 yuan per year. Teaching is mainly based on lectures, and students' tax rates are greatly reduced. In the future, a proper curriculum should be established and implemented effectively. 4. The original teaching duties of the school's faculty should be reassigned by the school's new principal after taking office, considering the circumstances, to facilitate reform. The order is issued to comply with and earnestly improve the report."

(2) Instruction to Private Huachun Association University, briefly stating: "The Ministry has previously sent personnel to inspect the school. According to the submitted report, after further review, the school's operations have a solid foundation, and the achievements of the medical and dental departments are particularly remarkable, which is commendable. However, the following points still need to be improved: 1. The College of Arts and Sciences has too many departments, but the number of students is very small. The school should draft a plan to cut and merge departments and submit it to the Ministry for approval. 2. The lectures designated by various established groups in the school fail to fully meet the needs of the school, and there are also courses that should be set up but do not have suitable teachers. The school president should be responsible for consulting with the board of directors to discuss appropriate improvement measures. As for the courses left behind during the faculty's vacations, efforts should be made to invite people to teach on their behalf to emphasize students' studies. 3. The school's faculty treatment should be based on qualifications. The current treatment of Chinese faculty is too low and should be improved immediately. 4. The school's administrative meeting should be reorganized in accordance with the current regulations of the University Organization Law, and professors and associate professors should elect representatives to attend. The order is issued to comply with and earnestly improve the report."

Chinese Physical Society Annual Meeting to be Held in Qingdao Starting the Day After Tomorrow

(Qingdao, 30th) The fourth annual meeting of the Chinese Physical Society will be held at Shandong University from September 2nd to 5th. Members from all over the country have arrived in Qingdao one after another.

National Academic Work Consultation Office to Establish a Shanghai Office Tomorrow to Handle Registration and Introduction Work for Graduates. Letters Sent to Universities and Organizations in the City for Information.

For the convenience of work, the National Academic Work Consultation Office has sent a letter to the China Vocational Education Society, requesting that the original office be changed to the Shanghai Office starting from September 1st, and that He Qingru, Pan Yangyao, and Yang Chonggao continue to be in charge. The office has decided to establish the office on the 1st and has sent a notice to universities and organizations. The notice is as follows: National Academic Work

Letter from the National Academic Consultation Office: The National Academic Work Consultation Office sent a letter to the China Vocational Education Society yesterday, stating that in order to promote work, the office plans to establish offices in major cities in China and has formulated regulations to facilitate implementation. The affairs of work consultation in Shanghai have always been entrusted to your society, but a formal name has not been specified, which is very inconvenient. It is now planned to handle the matter in accordance with the regulations and consult with your society to change the office to the Shanghai Office to unify the organization and facilitate progress. This matter concerns the convenience of both parties and is expected to be approved. As for the number and titles of staff in the office, there are no regulations in the regulations. If it is necessary to formulate them, a separate agreement should be made. As for the expenses and subsidies for office work, it is proposed to continue to handle them in accordance with the agreement in the office's letter No. 197 of December 26th of the 23rd year. A copy of the regulations for establishing offices by various organizations and groups entrusted by the office is enclosed for your information.

Regulations for Establishing Offices: The regulations for establishing offices by various organizations and groups entrusted by the National Academic Work Consultation Office are as follows: (1) In order to facilitate the registration and introduction of graduates from domestic colleges and universities, the office entrusts relevant educational and academic organizations and groups in major cities in China to establish offices. (2) Each office shall be called the National Academic Work Consultation [Location] Office. (3) Each office shall handle the following matters: A. Investigation of special events; B. Receiving and distributing investigation and registration forms from the Consultation Office; C. Holding interviews and talks with registrants and being responsible for recording them; D. Contacting industrial and technical organizations to provide internship sites for the office's registered personnel; E. Answering consultation matters; F. Contacting job introductions; G. Connecting with vocational introduction agencies in the local area. (4) Each entrusted organization or group should designate several staff members to handle all affairs of the office and report to the office for filing. (5) The office may, at its discretion, provide monthly subsidies for office expenses to each entrusted organization or group. (6) In addition to normal communication, each office should exchange routine letters with the office at least twice a week. (7) The establishment of offices by each entrusted organization or group shall be subject to a trial period of one year. During this period, they shall not request to terminate the office relationship on their own. After the expiration, they may continue to negotiate for an extension. (8) If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the office may negotiate with each entrusted organization or group at any time to make additional agreements.

The Shanghai Office Sends Letters to Universities: The Shanghai Office has decided to formally establish on September 1st. Yesterday, it sent separate letters to universities and organizations in the city, stating that the office previously received a letter from the National Academic Work Consultation Office, No. 197, entrusting the society to formulate five cooperative measures starting from January of the 24th year: (1) Matters concerning the investigation entrusted by the Consultation Office; (2) Receiving and distributing investigation and registration forms from the Consultation Office; (3) Introducing famous factories and consulting with the Consultation Office to discuss internship introduction measures; (4) Answering inquiries from the Consultation Office; (5) Handling matters related to the introduction of registered personnel from the Consultation Office in Shanghai. The society has entrusted the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center affiliated to it to handle the matter. In order to facilitate external liaison and unify the organization, the National Academic Work Consultation Office has instructed to change the name to the Shanghai Office of the National Academic Work Consultation Office, which will be affiliated to the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center starting from September 1st of the 24th year. The name of the Shanghai Office will be used to handle the affairs of the National Academic Work Consultation Office, while continuing all the original work and external relations of the society. This is hereby announced, and it is hoped that you will take note of it.

Municipal Bureau of Education to Hold Training Classes for Private School Teachers. Classes to Begin at 7 PM Tomorrow in Six Schools in Four Districts of the City.

The Municipal Bureau of Education has been instructed by the Ministry to hold training classes for private school teachers. Preparations have been completed, and classes will be opened in districts. Japanese Residents' Group Asks the Municipal Council to Increase Subsidies for Japanese Schools.

The Foreign Affairs Negotiation Committee of the Japanese Residents' Group in the city held a meeting the day before yesterday to discuss the issue of subsidies from the Municipal Council to American businesses. As a result, it was planned to request the Council to increase the subsidies appropriately. The reason given was that the Municipal Council's budget for this year provided an annual subsidy of 1,061,470 yuan for Chinese schools and 833,380 yuan for foreign schools. There are approximately 5,800 Chinese students and approximately 1,600 foreign students. The average amount per person is more than 520 yuan for foreigners and 183 yuan for Chinese. However, the schools set up by the Japanese Residents' Group have a total of approximately 4,000 faculty and students, and the Municipal Council only subsidized 128,000 yuan in the first half of the year, averaging just over 30 yuan per person. Therefore, it is considered that there is still room for an increase.

A group of eighteen people from the Political Observation Group of Zhongshan University in Guangzhou, led by Professor Ren Qishan, arrived in Shanghai yesterday on the Dollar Line's President Lincoln. Then they will take the road to Jinan and Qingdao to Wuhan and then Hangzhou. Then they will come to Shanghai to wait for a boat and return to Guangdong. The observation period is scheduled for one month.

Sports News

The Venue for the National Games has been Handed Over Yesterday. The Organizing Committee will Begin to Arrange the Venue and Equipment. There are Rumors that the Swimming Pool will Open on September 8th.

The construction of various projects at the Shanghai Grand Sports Stadium has been completed. The Municipal Government specially sent staff to hand over the sports stadium, gymnasium, and swimming pool to the Organizing Committee of the National Games yesterday. The committee specially sent Guo Yongxi, Jiang Xueqi, and Xie Guanshi to handle the handover. The gymnasium was received first at 10:00 AM last year, followed by the swimming pool, and the sports stadium was received in the afternoon. The handover was completed at 3:00 PM. The organizing committee is now preparing to arrange various equipment at the venue. The swimming pool was originally scheduled to open on August 24th, but it was postponed to September 1st due to the unfinished construction. It is now rumored that it will still be difficult to open on September 1st and has been rescheduled to open on September 8th, opening for one month. However, whether this is true remains to be verified. A reporter from Shanghai News Agency went to visit yesterday and saw that the scale of each construction project is grand and the equipment is perfect, worthy of being the best in the Far East. The general situation is divided as follows:

Sports Stadium: The area is 37,500 square meters. The stands around the stadium look like a city wall from a distance, extremely majestic. The stadium is 175 meters wide and 330 meters long, with a stand height of 10 meters and a seating capacity of 60,000 people. The center is the field event field and the football, volleyball, and national arts field. The grass has been laid. The surrounding track is 500 meters long and has also been completed. Only the ground outside the track is still being organized. Under the stands are the athletes' dormitory, temporary shopping mall, public restrooms, ticket offices, etc. The dormitory can accommodate 2,500 people, and the corridors are wide and easy to enter and exit. Other facilities such as rest rooms, offices, exhibition rooms, information desks, wireless broadcasting stations, and dining rooms are all available. There are large gates on the east and west sides of the stadium, with special stands above, specially for VIPs and newspaper reporters. There are also 20 telephones set up in the reporters' backstage for rent by various newspapers.

Gymnasium: Entering from the main entrance is the lobby, with ticket offices on both sides. Further in is the hall, with male and female restrooms on both sides, and stairs leading to the stands. Further in is the foyer, which leads directly to the sports hall and the fitness room, and next to the office and reception room. On both sides of the hall are the male and female athletes' changing rooms and shower rooms. The entire hall can accommodate 3,500 seats and 1,500 standing places. The hall is 23 meters wide and 40 meters long and can accommodate three ordinary basketball courts. During formal competitions, only a larger court is set up in the center. The white iron basketball stand is different from the ordinary ones. There are 48 electric lights installed at a high level. Because the four walls are white, the light is quite bright. Heating equipment is also available.

Swimming Pool: It can accommodate 5,000 to 6,000 spectators. Under the stands are separate male and female athletes' changing rooms and shower rooms. The pool is 50 meters long and 20 meters wide, with a shallow end of 1.24 meters and a deepest end of 3.38 meters. At the end is a diving platform and two diving [Platforms]. At the other end, there is a simple children's swimming pool. There are a total of 30 wall lamps in the pool. The water capacity is 600,000 gallons. The water filtration equipment is especially complete. There are three large water filtration pots. When dirty water enters the pot, it is first disinfected with soda and alum, then filtered in the pot, and then returned to the pool. The pool water is always clean without needing to be changed. It is the latest style of swimming pool.

Little Men (30) (1)

— Original by Ms. Louisa May Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

Another beneficial thing, but I don't know how it came about as if blown by a good wind for no reason. Several of the children are "doing business"—this is how they say it—because most come from poor families. Mr. and Mrs. Bhaer know that they will soon have to support themselves, so they encourage all kinds of efforts to become self-reliant. Tommy sells his eggs; Jack speculates in the livestock business; Franz helps with teaching and also gets a little tuition; Nat loves woodworking, so a lathe was set up for him. He used it to make many useful and beautiful things, which he sells; Little Joe builds small wheels "Wiggle-Waggle," (a kind of top,) and all kinds of useless but mysterious machines of various types that cannot be named. He also sells these to the other children.

"Let him be a mechanic, if he likes," Mr. Bhaer said. "Give each child a kind of trade, then he can be self-reliant. Work is beneficial to the body and mind, so no matter what talents these children have—whether it is poetry or farming—they must be cultivated, and if possible, be made into useful villagers."

One day, Ned ran in anxiously and hurriedly asked:

"A group of people in the forest are having a picnic. They invited me to play the piano for them. Can I go? They will give me a little money. I want to earn some money like the other children. Playing the piano is my only way to get money."

Mr. Bhaer immediately replied:

"Go, I am very happy to see this news. This is a pleasant and easy job for you. I am very happy to hear that they have given you this opportunity."

Financial Foreign Exchange Soars, Gold Price Suddenly Rises, Momentum Lacks Longevity, Popularity Still Good, Result Continues to Rise Nine Yuan

Yesterday, the gold market was stirred by the National Products Bank and other institutions' efforts to purchase foreign exchange, causing the price to rise. Some people predicted that it would approach 900 yuan, but unexpectedly, foreign banks' willingness to sell remained strong, and buyers unloaded their holdings, stopping the rising trend. Early in the morning, the overseas silver market saw British and American markets both flat, with Montelieri's forward silver price rising by 3 li and shrinking by 4 li. Exchange rates slightly contracted, and London spot gold rose by half a penny. People's hearts were still stable, and the pre-market trading opened, rising to 878 yuan. Richang, Dadecheng, Huixiang, and Hengyu sold high and retreated to 6 yuan. Huixiang, Fuxing, and Yong took advantage of the low prices to maintain the price, rising to 7 yuan. After opening, the market became idle. The Central Bank's listed prices were announced, with both British and American currencies flat and the customs gold unit unchanged. The listed standard price for gold was 923.5 yuan, and people's hearts were very calm. The market situation was extremely quiet. It was known that the HSBC Bank's listed prices also showed British and American currencies flat. At this time, sellers were strong, and the price once fell. However, due to the tightening of the foreign exchange market, buyers were still active, and the price soon rebounded. Although the Central Bank sold, general banks were happy to purchase and push up the price. However, due to HSBC selling British currency and MacCallum selling American currency, there was still much fluctuation. Finally, due to large buyers' purchases and the National Products Bank's purchases, the price broke through the 90 yuan mark. A rumor arose in the market that the Central Bank was opening for cash, and the price rose. Banks took advantage of the high price to sell. After the rise, the price stabilized for a while. The Hong Kong market weakened, and the Indian silver forecast fell by two annas. Large buyers continued to enter the market, and the foreign exchange market became even more difficult to settle. At noon, the rising momentum resumed strongly. Although the after-hours market was firm, it unexpectedly turned into a falling trend after opening, mainly because banks' real selling appetite was still strong. At the same time, due to the decline in public bonds, there was unnecessary concern in the market. In addition, Jewish merchants such as Qiao Zhifu all sold, and the market hardened. Large buyers unloaded their holdings, and the price softened rapidly. However, because banks took advantage of the low prices to purchase and sell, the low-priced trend gradually improved. Unfortunately, banks still sold at high prices. The first telegram from the Indian silver market reported unchanged prices and a shrinking of one anna, leading to a slight decline. The second report from India was flat. After this, people's hearts were settled, buying interest recovered, and the closing was stable. It can be seen that the market situation for the day was characterized by easy rises and difficult falls. However, most of the large buyers were speculative, and any change could lead to a rapid decline. The trend is uncertain, but people's hearts are still showing a positive outlook. Yarn and Cotton – Many Yarn and Cotton Self-Settlements

Yesterday was the settlement day for the August yarn futures, and the market was closed as usual. The August yarn futures were launched on the market on March 1st at a price of 184.2 yuan. The yarn market was turbulent because of the gold fraud storm, and business turnover suffered unfavorably. Foreign firms seized the opportunity to sell off day by day, and the yarn market fell into a slump. The lowest point of the August futures was 161 yuan, a step down of 23.1 yuan from the launch price. Fortunately, the current yarn sales suddenly became active. Factories were hit by frequent yarn price drops, and closures became more frequent, and reduced working hours became a more common phenomenon, resulting in a sharp reduction in output. Long positions took the opportunity to raise prices, and at the same time, rumors of inflation in the market were extremely strong, which further boosted the activities of long positions. The long-tired yarn market began to react violently, rising from the lowest of 161 yuan on July 2nd to 178.8 yuan on July 39th, a sharp increase of 17.8 yuan in 17 days. Market sentiment was boiling, but the rumors of inflation could not be confirmed. Current sales turned from boom to clear, and the once-excited yarn market fell into a tired path again. At the end of August, large long positions suddenly abandoned delivery and settled all positions. The market disk supported itself, and finally closed at 165.6 yuan, 18.6 yuan lower than the launch price, and 7.4 yuan lower than the July closing price. The remaining amount to be delivered was 1,600 bales, all of which were self-settled. The settlement price for the last three days was calculated at 167 yuan, which was 2 yuan lower than in July.

The cotton market was launched on March 1st at 35.75 yuan for the August cotton futures and quickly broke through the 6 yuan mark. However, due to the influence of financial depletion and the sharp decline in the yarn market, the cotton market gradually fell into a tired state. Factory shutdowns and production cuts became more and more serious, and current cotton sales felt even more sluggish. The falling trend could not be suppressed, and the lowest point of 30.035 yuan was seen on June 18th. However, the bulls, considering that although there was a large inventory of old cotton, most of it was in the hands of banks, and due to the loss, they were all strictly guarded and not released. The market solved the problem of having a large amount of spot cotton available for circulation, and took the opportunity to forcefully squeeze the shorts in the near term. The futures price also rose very quickly due to the flood. At the same time, inflation was reported, and the market sentiment was boiling for a time. The cotton market reacted and rose sharply, with the highest point being 36.9 yuan. Although the yarn market re-entered a tired path in mid-August due to untruthful rumors, the near-term cotton market remained strong due to the efforts of bulls to push it higher. Unfortunately, in the last three days, the U.S. government suddenly announced that this year's U.S. cotton loan was 9 points per 　, 3 points less than last year, and the world cotton market reported a sharp decline. It was not easy for the long position to pull, and they brought a small loss of 0.89 yuan and closed at 36 yuan, 0.15 yuan higher than the launch price, only 0.9 yuan lower than the highest price, and 0.5 yuan higher than in July. Chronicles

Tidbits

— (Wanlu)

The greatest joy in the world lies in seeking it from the greatest hardship. As the saying goes, "A wife is not as good as a concubine, a concubine is not as good as a maid, a maid is not as good as stealing, and stealing is not as good as being unable to steal." This perfectly illustrates these two sayings.

"Morality is declining," this saying has been passed down for countless years. If it were really declining like this every day, would there still be a world after all these years? I believe that this mentality of "doubting the present based on the past" is the root cause of China's weakness. In fact, the "decline" in "morality" seen from the perspective of conservatives may well be the progress of the world.

All the bad people in the world are forced out by the so-called good people. Without good people, so many bad people would not be created. The more good people there are, the more bad people there will be. I want to use Han Yu's words to say, "If good people do not die, bad people will not stop."

A Glimpse of National Character

— Zheng Yimei

Our national character is good at imitation and崇尙 hypocrisy, as evidenced by the two matters on the left side.

Rough-cut books are popular due to the prevalence of Western culture. A book publication can sell millions of copies. In some cases, the binding is barely finished before it has to be put on the market without being trimmed, so rough-cut books became popular. It was originally a necessary situation, and not because rough-cut books have any advantages. Unexpectedly, when such books came to our country, people thought that they were fashion and the book was imitated one another. The new books are mostly rough-cut books, but in fact, 60-70 percent of the population are illiterate, and there is more time than needed to be cut in a relaxed time. The situation is different, so why so hastily. When young students buy books back, they use a small knife and cut while reading, which they are not afraid of trouble. Instead, they think that it is not enough to add interest if this is not done.

Western artists with artists' hair. Because they focus on skills, they often left beard long hair without cutting, which is similar to the purpose of the previous celebrities. I did not expect that in recent years, there are some teenagers who deliberately keep long hair like messy grass, thinking that this is the style of an artist. How do these teenagers know anything about art? They live drunk dream and also imitate others and use the artist as an excuse. This is how ridiculous.

In the Tram

— Sigao

The tram stopped at Dongxin Bridge.

As it was about to start, a very modern young woman boarded, clutching a small handbag and carrying a small fancy paper umbrella, even though the sun had long set below the horizon.

The tram was not empty to begin with. I and two other passengers were standing. This stop added several more people, making it seem crowded. This young woman stood beside me—no one offered her a seat—and a fragrance wafted over. I have always disliked that kind of scented powder, perfume, and essence, so I glared at her. Little did I know that this was where the incident would unfold.

Thinking that I wasn't paying attention, she took a letter out of her small handbag and deliberately dropped it on the floor, not picking it up for a long time. Two stops later, the tram became less crowded and I sat down. She immediately sat close beside me. After a while, she suddenly seemed to discover something and hurriedly picked up the letter. Turning to me, she looked up with a sweet smile and said, "Sir, you dropped your letter!" All the while acting coquettishly.

I casually took it and saw "Please Open" scrawled on the envelope in pen. Suddenly realizing the potential trouble, I immediately called the conductor over. Smiling, I said, "Someone must have lost this letter here. Take it to the lost and found!" With that, I handed the letter to him. The conductor also smiled, glancing at the envelope, then at her, then at me.

As a result, everyone in the tram started paying attention to her, making her so uncomfortable that she couldn't sit still. At the next stop, she hurried off as if she had lost something. In my heart, I thought, "That was a close call!"

Foreigner

— Hualing

A new family has moved into our building this time. Although the people in this family all have yellow skin and black hair, the men wear long gowns and the women wear qipaos, just like us, on the day they moved in, they were given the title of "foreigner."

The reason is that according to Shanghai custom, when a new family moves in, everyone, regardless of age, has to light a pair of candles to heaven and earth when they enter the house. However, this family refused to light them. They said, "Although we are not religious, we don't believe in these things either. If you insist that we light incense and candles, we would rather not rent this house." As a result, the other residents whispered about this family having "foreigner" habits.

On the second night after they moved in, the other residents were playing mahjong until 10:30 PM, and the "foreigner" came out to interfere, saying that it was too noisy to sleep. They didn't greet the other residents much when they came in or out. If a female resident went to their room, they would solemnly ask, "What is your business?" If they couldn't state their business, they would be treated coldly.

The owner of the house had a younger brother who had lost his job and came to borrow money from his older brother. The older brother put on a stern face and refused. He said, "Although we are brothers, you also have the ability to be self-reliant. If I continue to support you, I would only be fostering your dependence. When his younger brother wanted to say something, he simply flicked his sleeves and went upstairs. As a result, the other residents gained an even deeper understanding of this "foreigner."

World News

Tea Party in the Sky

— Xi

Nowadays, a kind of tea party is very popular in Shanghai's social circle. Whenever a send-off and welcome some important people to go abroad and return to China, they often hold a grand tea party to show respect. However, this kind of tea party is always held in large hotels or private gardens, which is not as good as the Westerners' holding a tea party in the sky.

In September 1931, twenty men and women in London, England, took a car from the city center to Kroydon Airport. They first toured this famous airport for a week, and then sat on the Royal large plane for a half-hour flight, during which they held an air tea party. Its strong interest is really above any tea party on the ground, creating the newest page in the history of London aviation.

According to one of the twenty people, Mr. Pude, he himself said the situation at that time, which is very valuable to record. He said:

"When we gathered in the hall of Kroydon Airport, everyone's face showed a tense expression, not even a smile. We were all speculating about the experience in the next half an hour. It must be laughable in the eyes of many people who take long-distance flights.

"The first exciting thing for us was to see the big monster lying there, which we will borrow as a living room for tea parties. It is called the 'Coventry City' and is an aircraft with twenty seats, often flying in the sky all over Europe. A small team of mechanics, like ants, climbed on various parts of it, making final checks and adjustments.

"Suddenly, a roar startled us so much that we almost ran out of the airport and back to London. It turned out that the propellers of the three large engines on the plane had started to rotate, emitting a roar-like sound. We were ordered to enter the plane and take our seats.

"We climbed into a small door near the tail of the plane and saw a small room like a subway car, but both sides were single seats, and there was a narrow aisle in the middle. The windows on both sides were open, and we could see everything up and down very comfortably.

"Finally, our plane paralleled a journey on the ground, and then gradually rose. We started flying.

"Most of us twenty people were flying for the first time. Although experts say that the national interest in airplanes is increasing day by day, ordinary people feel that flying is always a very exciting thing.

"The rattling sound of the engine was deafening, so we could no longer talk. We could only see the expressions on each other's faces to know how excited everyone was. The most interesting thing was that ten female guests who usually talked and laughed were all speechless and could not say a word. So, this half hour, we seemed to be holding a dumb tea party.

"We flew to a top speed. During these few minutes, it was almost impossible to see the people in the parks and streets below. On the way back to London, the first thing we saw was the famous Crystal Palace, but because it flew so high, it looked flat, as if it were painted on the ground.

"I was just glancing at the Tower Bridge when I suddenly felt someone tap me on the shoulder. It turned out that the refreshments were ready. A steward in uniform handed me a cup of tea and asked loudly in my ear, 'Sir, do you want one sugar or two sugars? Do you want something else to eat?' I replied loudly, 'Please give me one sugar, oh! Sorry, I don't want to eat anything else.' At this time, we had flown high to more than three thousand feet.

"The biggest stimulus we received this afternoon was that between the turning of the aircraft, we saw a large wing suddenly rising, and everything on the ground flew away like lightning. We stopped to see that the plane had turned a body.

"Although we had been in the sky for half an hour, it was as fast as half a minute. We only heard the sound of the engine gradually decreasing. After a while, we were already over Croydon and began to descend. All the houses, trees and human beings have been restored to their original shape. We grazed over the lawn for a few seconds before stopping in front of the airplane shed.

"When we came down from the aircraft, ten cigarette cases were taken out from the pockets of ten male guests at the same time, and ten small cigarettes were put on ten mouths at the same time. It turned out that we had not been close to it for half an hour. We were interested in everything at this tea party in the sky. The only regret was that there were no cigarettes to smoke, because our hostess, Miss Aircraft, absolutely did not allow people to smoke."

Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Superheterodyne Beat Frequency Oscillator

— KMK

Whether it is a superheterodyne receiver or a regenerative receiver, its optimal efficiency and sensitivity occur when the detection vacuum tube is about to oscillate but has not yet become strong. Therefore, wireless technology in certain applications requires a balanced oscillating current generated by a vacuum tube to achieve its full potential and optimal efficiency. Although the oscillator's active component is a single (diode or triode) vacuum tube, achieving balanced oscillations of varying strengths depends entirely on the inductor coils in the plate circuit and grid circuit. Thus, the inductance of the coil is even more important in the oscillator, requiring more meticulous design.

The "Superheterodyne Beat Frequency Oscillator" introduced in this article is one of the easiest types to design for superheterodyne radios. Many Hawk King radios from 1933 to 1934 used this type of oscillator for its ease of manufacturing and stable efficiency, as shown in the attached diagram. The active oscillation point of the oscillator is assumed to be the cathode and plate of the first detection vacuum tube. The oscillator's oscillation coil is series-connected (located externally to avoid affecting its selectivity) to save design and manufacturing trouble. The outer diameter of the paper tube is 1 1/4 inches, wound with 34-gauge American Standard enameled wire: 5 turns between A and B, 42 turns between B and C, and 6 turns between C and D (totaling 53 turns). The coil must be shielded (see the dashed lines around it in the diagram). C is a 0.00036 MFD variable capacitor. C1 and C3 are both 0.00005 MFD (high-quality insulation) fixed capacitors. C2 is a 0.1 MFD fixed capacitor with a voltage rating of 400 volts or higher. R is a 650-ohm fixed resistor. R1 consists of two 50,000-ohm fixed resistors connected in series, capable of passing 2 watts of power or more, otherwise it will easily overheat. After the device is made, if the oscillation current is still too strong or weak, simply replace the capacitance of C3 with a larger or smaller value. There is no need to change the inductance of the coil.

New Vacuum Tube Similar to All-Metal Vacuum Tube in Properties

— Pao

Since General Electric announced its "All-Metal Vacuum Tube," American radio manufacturers have paid close attention, even leading to legal disputes. Each related manufacturer is working in the shadows to gain a foothold in this emerging market. Recently, the manufacturer of "Arcturus" vacuum tubes has introduced a novel vacuum tube whose characteristics and base connections are exactly the same as those of all-metal tubes. The only difference is that it still uses the old-style glass bulb.

The naming principle of this type of vacuum tube is the same as that of all-metal tubes, but it is followed by the letter G (the first letter of "Glass") for distinction. For example, "6K7G" indicates a glass bulb vacuum tube with the same characteristics and base connections as the 6K7 all-metal vacuum tube. Its appearance is shown in the attached diagram, with the glass type on the left and the shadow of an all-metal type on the right.

This type of vacuum tube already manufactured and available on the market includes pentagrid frequency converter tubes, general-purpose triodes, triode output tubes, high-mu triodes, pentode output tubes, dual plate tubes, pentode high gain tubes, pentode detection tubes, pentagrid mixer tubes, and full-wave rectifier tubes. The wide variety is sufficient for general use.

Although all-metal vacuum tubes are being manufactured in large quantities, there are still significant technical issues. However, this type of glass bulb has past experience in manufacturing ordinary vacuum tubes to rely on, making manufacturing as easy as riding a familiar road. It is heard that several radio manufacturers have already started manufacturing radios using this type of vacuum tube.

New 1B5 Direct-Current Dual Plate Triode Vacuum Tube

— Zhi

Recently, Hygrad Sylvania Corporation in the United States released a new direct-current power-saving dual plate triode tube, tube type 1B5.

The 1B5 vacuum tube consists of a triode section and a dual plate section, suitable for use in direct-current superheterodyne radios as a second detector, amplifier, and automatic volume control, etc. The triode section and the dual plate, except for the filament that emits electrons, are absolutely unrelated to each other, so it is like using two vacuum tubes in the circuit without any difficulty.

In practice, the structure of the 1B5 is actually the same as the AC vacuum tubes 55, 75, and 85, only that the filament is powered by direct current, so no cathode equipment is needed.

Its characteristics are as follows:

Filament Voltage 2 volts

Filament Current 0.06 amps

Plate Voltage 135 volts

Plate Current 0.8 milliamperes

Grid Voltage Negative 3 volts

Plate Resistance 35,000 ohms

Transconductance 575 micromhos

Amplification Factor 20

Amateur Musings

— Wu Yingjian

When listening to shortwave, it is often easy to miss weak shortwave stations. Because these weak signals do not have the surging sound wave that is emitted in the loudspeaker or earphone in the broadcast band, it is easy to overlook them. Recently, a vacuum tube device has become popular in the United States. It can help shortwave radios find weak shortwave stations and has a special effect when used in heterodyne shortwave radios (not suitable for high-frequency amplified ones). The latest heterodyne shortwave radios in the United States already have this device, called "Beat Oscillator" in English. When this device is connected to a heterodyne shortwave radio, and the switch is turned on, and the radio's dial is turned to a weak shortwave station, the radio immediately emits a hissing sound. If the dial is continued to be turned and passes the station, the hissing sound will immediately stop. Therefore, with this device, weak shortwave stations are very easy to receive and will not be missed. As long as the hissing sound occurs in the radio, then turn off the switch of this machine, and the station's broadcast can be heard in the loudspeaker or earphone. However, one point must be paid attention to, that is, if the radio's intermediate frequency is 456 kilocycles (456KC), then this machine must be calibrated to 466 kilocycles. In other words, it must exceed the original machine by one thousand cycles, otherwise it will not have any effect. Because in this way, a one thousand cycle sound can be obtained, because the original two frequencies (456KC and 456KC) cannot be heard, while a one thousand cycle sound can be heard by the human ear.

The attached diagram is the circuit of this device, using two No. 37 triode tubes. One end is the power inlet line, which can be connected to 110 volt AC or DC. The other end is the intermediate frequency amplifier tube or the grid of the second detector tube of the heterodyne shortwave radio. After this machine is connected to the radio, in addition to the above-mentioned function, it has no other effect on the radio at all. Other components have been noted in the circuit diagram and will not be described separately.

Remote Control Volume Adjuster

— Lu Zhimin

A volume adjuster is essential in ordinary radios, and new radios have automatic volume adjusters. But this is not the normal situation, because many radios do not have this equipment, maybe even ordinary volume adjusters on the radio. Even ordinary volume adjusters are very convenient to use. If you are sitting far away from the radio listening quietly, and suddenly encounter a loud, ear-piercing sound, you have to walk to the radio to adjust it, which is very troublesome. But if you have a remote volume control next to your seat, you can comfortably sit in your seat and gently turn the adjuster, and the ear-piercing sound will immediately turn into a soft tone from the loudspeaker. Because remote control volume adjusters have this advantage, here is an introduction to a remote control volume adjuster used on a motorized loudspeaker, as shown in Figure 1, using a potentiometer (40 ohms) connected in parallel with the voice coil and the secondary of the output transformer. You can put the potentiometer in a beautiful small wooden box, and connect the wires with long flower wires for easy movement. The connection method in Figure 1 is more ingenious than using a variable resistor as in Figure 2. It can also make the tone quality more beautiful, but some loudspeakers need to be connected with a 20 ohm potentiometer to get good results.

All-Wave Radio

— Pao

A radio that can receive the shortwave band from more than ten meters to two hundred meters, and the broadcast band from two hundred meters to five hundred and fifty meters, is an "all-wave radio".

Because of the increase in shortwave broadcasting stations, there are currently many types of all-wave radios on the market. It can be predicted that future radios will tend to be all-wave due to factual needs.

The reason why all-wave radios have not been manufactured in large quantities for a long time is actually due to a prejudice. The method of changing bands in original all-wave radios can usually be divided into two types: A) Using plug-in coils to change the inductance in the tuning circuit; B) Using a switching arrangement to achieve the same purpose. Method B is simple to install and convenient to use, far surpassing Method A, but some people believe that its effectiveness is not as good as Method A. This is actually a major obstacle to the development of all-wave radios. But in fact, if designed properly, Method B is not inferior to Method A.

Amateur shortwave radios have many devices obtained through experience, or will be universally installed on all-wave radios due to the need for facts. For example: using an extremely detailed scale so that one-tenth of a degree can still be distinguished by sight; using an easy-to-tune "band amplification" device; using a "antenna circuit tuning capacitor" that can exert maximum effectiveness; and illuminating the scale to make reading the numbers quick and accurate. These devices all have the true value of facilitating the reception of shortwave signals, and are worth installing on all-wave radios.

When receiving shortwave signals, the "fading" phenomenon is particularly obvious, the signal is sometimes strong and sometimes weak, even sometimes present and sometimes absent. Therefore, automatic volume control is also an indispensable device for the all-wave radio of the era. Regarding this device, there are many people who are currently engrossed in research. In the future, all-wave radios will have more perfect automatic volume control equipment, so that the volume can always remain unchanged, to overcome this hateful fading phenomenon.

Outlook

— Spring

According to a survey by the "Gold Yuan Kingdom" authorities, North America has 19,769,045 radio receivers and 839 radio stations. Recent progress in European radio has also been rapid, with a total of 18,572,380 radio receivers and 276 radio stations in Europe. Worldwide, there are a total of 42,516,904 radio receivers and 1,694 radio stations.

Among European countries, Germany has made the fastest progress in radio broadcasting recently. It is estimated that the number of listeners increased by 300,000 in January of this year alone. This is because Germany is enthusiastically promoting national radios, aiming to make radio universally accessible throughout the country in the short term. Goebbels, the Minister of Propaganda of the National Socialist Party, once said: "Only radio is the only bridge connecting the government and the people, and a powerful tool for educating the people." (The national radio is a very low-cost radio designed by the German government to make radio universally accessible, with each unit costing approximately 76 marks.)

According to a survey by Dr. Starch in the United States, 800,000 automobiles were equipped with radios last year. Over 2,295,770 households in the United States have more than two radios. Listeners with a monthly income of around $200 are the most numerous, followed by farmers.

Canadian authorities have recently banned radio stations from broadcasting advertising programs on Sundays.

In European countries, radio broadcasting is generally controlled by the government, and radio stations rely on listener fees for funding. However, the United States is the opposite. Listeners do not have to pay listener fees, and radio stations rely solely on broadcasting advertisements to generate revenue for expenses. The total advertising revenue in the United States last year was estimated at 73 million US dollars.

The radio station with the greatest power in the world is the Moscow Radio Station in the Soviet Union, with 500 kW. There is also a 500 kW radio station in New Sienna, USA, but it is only for experimental use.

Publishing World

### The Great Wave of Chinese Thought

— Murofushi Takanobu

Here I will talk about the "January 10th Declaration." The so-called January 10th Declaration refers to the declaration of January 10th. On January 10th of this year, ten of China's leading professors, including Tao Xisheng and Sa Mengwu, issued a joint declaration. This is the so-called declaration for the construction of a Chinese-centric culture.

Prior to this, in March of last year, the China Cultural Construction Association was established, with branches established in Shanghai, Fujian, Hebei, and Gansu. In October, a magazine called "Cultural Construction" was published. This joint declaration by ten professors was published in this magazine and in Shanghai's leading newspaper, the Shen Bao, and other newspapers, immediately stirring up nationwide excitement. Almost every contemporary Chinese scholar or thinker has discussed this issue, and the Chinese intellectual world is now centered on this issue, showing a new development.

The so-called "January 10th Declaration" by the ten professors is, in some respects, very compromising, skeptical, and seems to be looking left and right, lacking a central grasp. Perhaps this precisely represents the general tragedy of intellectuals who grew up in modern education. In this regard, this declaration, as Cai Yuanpei said, is nothing special, and as Hu Shi said, it is a new disguise for old ideas; however, the waves it has stirred up are enormous. From this, we see the clash of eras.

The January 10th Declaration emphasizes "here and now" and strives to establish a foothold in reality and the direction of this reality. This is very different from simple retrospective thinking and reactionism. Moreover, they also demand something different, such as "not adhering to the old" and "not blindly following." Later, they further said, "Review the past, grasp the present, and create the future."

From this point of view, there are no new suggestions or critical things in their declaration, and no issues have been raised. Indeed, this can be seen as a kind of Darwinian theory of evolution or Hegelian theory of development, but in today's world, there seems to be no need for a declaration.

They then explained themselves, adopting the strengths and discarding the weaknesses, and choosing the good and following it. This is what Confucius called "When walking with two others, I can always find a teacher." As Hu Shi said, in this regard, the declaration has not surpassed Kang Youwei and Liang Qichao by a single step. However, before criticizing the declaration, we must grasp its overall significance, which is its meaning of the era.

The key point of the January 10th Declaration is to emphasize Chinese culture or Chinese-centric culture, which goes without saying. The declaration says, "In the realm of culture, we cannot see China today." China has disappeared into a thick fog, groping in the dark, unable to reach the sky above or the ground below, drifting and wandering in a realm of nothingness. This is the case in politics, economy, society, and thought.

"If China is to raise its head in the realm of culture," the declaration continues, "then politics, society, and thought must all have Chinese characteristics," that is, the construction of a Chinese-centric culture. China is China, so it must create culture based on its own uniqueness.

The problem lies here. The creation of a Chinese-centric national culture is the key point and the point of contention. And the reason why it has stirred up such a huge wave is also in this point.

They talk about reviewing the past, about a critical attitude, and about scientific methods, in order to emphasize "here and now." But this so-called "here and now" refers to China, so the so-called reviewing the past is longing for the heritage of the past, comparing the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods to the Greek and Roman cultures of European history. They want to use this history as a foundation, grasp China's "here and now," and thereby create a culture unique to China. In the waves of world culture, they look back on their past, awaken themselves, reflect on themselves, and after a long record of imitation and translation, continue their own re-evaluation in order to create themselves.

Since Zeng Guofan and Li Hongzhang introduced Western civilization, China, although not as rapidly as Japan, has been moving towards modernization. Especially from the World War to the Northern Expedition around 1927, China moved towards modernization with great momentum. The Chinese intellectual world, of course, could not be outside of this.

During this period, there were two great thinkers, Kang Youwei and Liang Qichao, who, in the great wind of Westernism, warned China not to lose itself and demanded that the people respect the heritage of their own Chinese culture. But they were only John, not Christ. "The sheep did not listen to their voice," and the times buried them in the camp of "reactionary thinkers," and moved forward towards licking the dregs of Western thought.

The eight years of Kuomintang rule in China were a good trial. This trial is still continuing. Whether China can withstand this trial is not the issue, but from this era, a lesson has been learned, which seems to be beyond doubt. At least the era of blindly worshipping the West is now over, which is a definite fact. The Chinese-centric cultural movement represents a new transformation of Chinese thinkers and, at the same time, the lives of the Chinese people. (Translated by Yi Yu from Yomiuri Shimbun, August 23rd)

### Several Things to Pay Attention to When Reviewing Publications

— Zhang Sumin

We not only hope for more publications but also for better ones. The quality of publications depends on the method of reviewing them. Therefore, from the publisher's point of view, reviewing publications is an extremely important matter. As far as I know, publishers should pay attention to at least the following when reviewing publications:

1. Pay Attention to the Text — The words to be printed on paper cannot be "careless." Before the vernacular movement became popular in China, the writing in all books and newspapers was quite remarkable. Regardless of the content, the writing was always fluent. Taking magazines as an example, the writing in Liang Qichao's Yong Yan, Guofeng, and Da Zhonghua, and Zhang Xingyan's Jia Yin was good. Even the writing in Liu Shifu's Minsheng Weekly, which promoted anarchism, was excellent. Since the popularization of vernacular Chinese, it seems that everyone can write books and articles. As a result, although the number of books and newspapers has increased, there are very few with good writing. I am not advocating classical Chinese and opposing vernacular Chinese, nor am I promoting literature. I am saying that the writing printed in books and newspapers, whether in classical or vernacular Chinese, must at least be fluent and understandable to the reader. Modern English, although vernacular, is treated very seriously in English and American books and magazines. English and American publishers immediately return manuscripts with even slight flaws in the writing. As a result, contributors have developed the habit of having their writing revised before submitting it if they know it is not very good. The publications with the worst writing in China today are translated books or papers. The reason is that the translators have not deeply understood the language they are translating from and have not thoroughly studied the science discussed in the books or papers they are translating. Publishers only see that the title of the book or paper is fashionable and do not make the effort to review and proofread it word by word, so they print such manuscripts. If readers do not believe this, try randomly picking a translated book or a translated article in a magazine and reading it carefully. You will surely find many confusing places. If you compare it to the original text, you will find many errors. There are indeed good translations, but I dare say that specialized and advanced books translated in China today, such as Marshall's Principles of Economics published by a certain bookstore, are unreadable. This is because Marshall's book is already difficult to read in the original, and translating it into Chinese is not an easy task. To translate such a book, one must have a special study of Marshall, just like the Englishman William Smart translating Austrian scholar Böhm-Bawerk's "Positive Theory of Capital." That bookstore casually accepting such a translation not only lacks common sense but also pays too little attention to the review of the writing in the manuscript. In short, publishers should first pay attention to the conciseness and fluency of the writing when reviewing manuscripts, whether they are original works, compilations, or translations.

2. Pay Attention to Content — After publishers review a manuscript and find the writing to be fluent, they should then examine its content. The so-called content includes many things, such as whether the material is rich and what its sources are, whether the analysis is precise and what its methods are, and whether the conclusion is correct and what its logic is. Other considerations include whether the allocation of chapters and sections is appropriate, whether the facts cited are based on evidence, whether the books referenced are listed, whether the arguments before and after are consistent, and whether the terms and private nouns used are consistent. There are indeed good publications in China in recent years, but most of them have incomplete content. There are also many with terribly bad content. Therefore, I hope that publishers will pay close attention to the content of publications in the future.

3. Pay Attention to Proofreading — The thread-bound books published in China in the past were carefully proofread and had very few errors. The same is true for books in Western countries today, with the principle of no errors being the norm and one or two errors being the exception. However, most of the books published in China recently have many errors, which shows the negligence of proofreading. I believe that the reason for this error is not entirely due to the typesetters, nor entirely due to the proofreaders, but to the sloppiness of the original manuscript. The old books we used to have few errors because we used to emphasize regular script and calligraphy. A manuscript submitted for printing was never sloppy. The reason why there are few errors in Western books is also because the manuscript submitted for printing has been typed very clearly by a typewriter. Try taking a handwritten English manuscript to any foreign printing shop, and they will not print it for you. To avoid too many printing errors, I think publishers can require authors to transcribe the manuscript neatly before submitting it for printing. If there are still errors, the proofreader should be responsible.

I think: A publication with fluent writing, perfect content, and no misprints is a publication that is not a waste of effort from the publisher's point of view, and it is naturally satisfying to the contributor. I wonder what publishers think of these simple words.

### Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems

— Zhao Jingshen

Published by Kaiming Bookstore, actual price 1.2 yuan

This book, compiled by Mr. Chen Naigan, is very useful for those who study lyric poetry. Ten years ago, the most easily available collection of Yuan Dynasty lyric poetry was only a copy of the Yuan edition of "Chaoye Xinsheng Taiping Yuefu" reprinted by the Commercial Press. Although it was a true Yuan edition, the handwriting was extremely rough and densely arranged, making it unpleasant to read. Moreover, the repetition of names and the mistaken inclusion of tunes easily lead people down the wrong path. For example, the "Taiping Yuefu Surname" at the beginning includes both Liu Shizhong and Liu Buzhai; both Wu Renqing and Wu Kezhai; both Zeng Ruiqing (i.e., Zeng Rui) and Zeng Hefu; both Wang Aishan and Wang Jingfu. Such errors of treating one person as two people do not exist in "Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems." Liu Shizhong does not have any short lyric poems. Others, such as Wu Renqing, Zeng Rui, and Wang Aishan, are only referred to by their names and have not been divided into two people.

In terms of tunes, Taiping Yuefu also has many errors. For example, Lu Zhi's Jiejiegao is classified as Xianlü in Taiping Yuefu Volume 5, but as Huangzhong in Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems; Zuitaiping is classified as Nanlü in Taiping Yuefu Volume 5, but as Zheng Gong in Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems; Guan Hanqing's Baihezi is classified as Shuangdiao in Taiping Yuefu Volume 3, but as Zheng Gong in Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems; Yibaner is classified as Huangzhong in Taiping Yuefu Volume 5, but as Xianlü in Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems; Maihuasheng is classified as Shuangdiao in Taiping Yuefu Volume 2, but as Zhonglü in Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems. Checking Dong Kang's Qu Mu Yun Bian (which is presumably compiled based on books such as Jiugong Dacheng Pu), all agree with Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems and disagree with Taiping Yuefu. Although the second pattern of Maihuasheng is classified as Shuangdiao, the four untitled poems by Xu Deke, the Haierxiangcha by Qiao Ji, and the poems on the seat, occasional poems, nostalgic poems, Sishi Lexing, and Ke Kuang by Zhang Kejiu collected by Taiping Yuefu and Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems all use the correct pattern or the first pattern. Li Yuanyu's Bei Ci Guang Zhi Pu Volume 5 Zhonglü Palace also contains the second nostalgic poem by Zhang Kejiu, which further proves that this pattern of 777447 is the correct pattern of Maihuasheng and should belong to Zhonglü, not Shuangdiao.

Ren Ne's San Qu Gailun (San Qu Congkan No. 14) lists 50 tunes exclusively for short lyric poems, 69 tunes for both short lyric poems and suites, and 34 tunes in the style of "taking over" tunes, for a total of 153 tunes. Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems only contains 99 tunes, but several of them are not included in Ren Ne's book, such as Zheng Gong Tuobushan, Xianlü Nazha Ling, Que Ta Zhi, Qing Ge'er, Siji Hua, Zhonglü Zuichunfeng, Shangdiao Baizi Zhiqiuling, Shuangdiao Yiding Yin, etc. The strangest thing is that Ren's book has "Tuobushan Takes Xiaoliangzhou" but no Tuobushan; it has "Nazha Ling Takes Que Ta Zhi" but no "Nazha Ling" and "Que Ta Zhi"; it has "Houtinghua Takes Qing Ge'er" but no "Qing Ge'er." Ren's book classifies Maihuasheng as Shuangdiao and Jiejiegao as Xianlü, presumably having been fooled by Taiping Yuefu.

Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems also appropriately classifies Liuyaobian as Xianlü. The original poem is only Qiao Ji's "Self-Description":

I don't compete for the top spot in the imperial examinations, I don't enter the biographies of famous and virtuous men. I am a wine saint at all times, a poetry Chan everywhere. A champion of smoke and clouds, a drunken immortal of the rivers and lakes. Chatting and laughing is the editorial board, lingering, criticizing the wind and cutting the moon for forty years.

The example given in Volume 3 of Bei Ci Guang Zheng Pu Xianlü Palace Liuyaobian is Zhu Tingyu's "Lovely Mid-Autumn":

The bright silver plate surges, the ice wheel moves. Boundless glass. No trace, no sign. Tonight is the best, how can the coming night be the same? Lingering and reluctant, Chang'e accompanies and serves, the heavens, don't let the shadow disappear and turn into the wutong tree.

It is almost exactly the same as Qiao Ji's "Self-Description"; the only difference is that Qiao Ji's first line is ten characters and two lines, while Zhu Tingyu's is seven characters per line. This is just adding embellishments. It can be seen that Qiao Ji's Liuyaobian should indeed be classified as Xianlü. Ren's book classifies Liuyaobian as Zheng Gong, which is another tune, also called Liushaoqing.

Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems is accompanied by an index of names, with a total of 93 families; arranged by tune, with a total of 99 tunes. This allows us to know how many people wrote short lyric poems in the Yuan Dynasty, how many commonly used tunes there were, and at a glance, we can know the general situation of Yuan Dynasty short lyric poems.

Unfortunately, Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems does not have a catalogue of the books used in the compilation. I hope he can add it in the second edition. At the same time, I also eagerly hope that Mr. Chen can compile a "Collection of Yuan Dynasty Suites" after Collection of Yuan Dynasty Short Lyric Poems to complete this work of "Complete Yuan Dynasty Songs."
